use a PWGSC appropriation/authority to issue Standing Advances, they must first seek PWGSC approval to use this authority.</p><p>Temporary Advances which departments issue during the year are charged to their operating or program appropriation. Those 
advances still outstanding at year-end are credited back against the operating or program appropriation and are charged 
against a special "H" authority in order to carry them over to the next year. The entry is reversed in the New Year. The 
only temporary advances that should be carried over for authority purposes are those which are for travel either in the 
New Year or which span both fiscal years.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li>FAA-Section 38</li><li>Accountable Advance Regulations</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Issuance of Standing advance</h4><p>An employee is issued a standing advance of $5,000. Subsequently, expenses of $3,978.56 are incurred, at which time, 
a claim is submitted for reimbursement. It is later decided that the amount of the standing advance is excessive and is 
reduced to $4,000.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) A standing advance is issued to an employee for $5,000.00 by way of an RG cheques.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Standing advances</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13315</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>H181</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5030</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop">
CR Accounts payable</th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>Note: There are further entries required to discharge the accounts payable. Please refer to the Accounts Payable section.</p></div><p><strong>FRA Rationale:</strong> In order to record and control the amount advanced to the employee, the financial asset 
account "Standing advances" is debited. It is basically a type of receivable, which is included under Loans, Investments 
and Advances.</p><p><strong>Authority Rationale:</strong> Since the authority to charge these payments comes from the PWGSC Working Capital 
Loan Vote L15b, authority code H181 is used. As accounts payable do not affect an appropriation, R300 is used.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> "5030 - Acquisition of other advances with cash" is used since the object classification 
identifies the nature of the transaction (i.e. to provide an advance to an employee - an outside party). The appropriate 
objects to identify the type of goods or services acquired will be charged when the advance is reimbursed. "6299 - Net Increase 
or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" is used to establish an accounts payable.</p><p>2) The employee incurs expenses of $3,978.56 and submits a request for reimbursement.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Operating expenses</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3,718.28</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>xxxx</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR GST refundable advance</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>260.28</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13392</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>G111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8171</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3,978.56</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Rationale:</strong> Since standing advances are operated on the Imprest System, any reimbursement of disbursements 
from the Standing Advance is reflected as an operating expense. The reimbursement to the holder replenishes the Standing 
advance to its original amount. Since the employee paid GST on his purchases, this amount should be recorded to the GST 
refundable advance account. Any PST paid is included with operating expenses.</p><p><strong>Authority Rationale:</strong> The expenses, claimed by the Standing Advance holder, are a legitimate charge against 
a departmental appropriation. Depending on the vote structure of the particular department, B11A or B12A is appropriate. 
There could be other Authority Codes used for different Scenario s e.g. if the expenses were to be recorded against a Specified 
Purpose Account (SPA). Since GST is not to be charged to a departmental appropriation, it is set up as an advance under 
a special authority G111.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> The objects to be used depend on the nature of the expenses incurred when the standing 
advance was reimbursed to its original amount. Departments should code the total of all individual transactions under $100 
in the same manner as the policy for purchases procured by acquisition cards. "6299 - Net Increase or Decrease to Other 
Liability Accounts" is used to establish or increase an accounts payable. Since there is GST/HST on the purchases, the GST 
must be reflected by using "8171 - Payment of GST on purchases"</p><p>3) It is decided that the amount of the standing advance is excessive and is reduced to $4,000</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Cash in Hands of Depts awaiting deposit to RG</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11125</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Standing advances</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13315</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>H181</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5035</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Rationale:</strong> Since the amount that the person is responsible for has been reduced, the financial asset 
account "Standing Advances" must be reduced and is thus credited to reflect the payment from the holder.</p><p><strong>Authority Rationale:</strong> Since the authority for Standing Advance flows through the PWGSC Working Capital 
Loan Vote, L15b, this account must be credited. This is done by using authority code H181. The Cash in Hands of Depts awaiting 
deposit to RG does not affect an appropriation so R300 is used.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> To record the net impact on Cash Accounts, 5299 would be used. "5035 - Settlement 
other advances with cash" is used to record either the full or partial reduction of a Standing Advance.</p><h4>Scenario B - Issuance of Trip advance</h4>
1) An employee is issued a trip advance of $1,000. Subsequently, the following independent scenarios occur: <p>2a) claim 
is submitted for $1,107.10;</p><p>2b) a claim is submitted for $ 937.89;</p><p>2c) the advance is still outstanding at year-end but travel is completed; and,</p><p>2d) the advance is still outstanding at year-end because the travel will not be completed until the New Year.</p><p>1) An employee is issued a trip advance for $1,000.00 by way of a RG cheque.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong> </strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Accountable advances</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13314</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5032</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>Note: there are further entries required to discharge the accounts payable. Please refer to the Accounts Payable section.</p></div><p><strong>FRA Rationale:</strong> In order to control and record the amount advanced to the employee, the financial asset 
"Accountable Advance" must be debited.</p><p><strong>Authority Rationale:</strong> Depending on the vote structure of the department, the trip advance would be charged 
against the department's program vote B11A or the operating vote B12A at the time the advance is made. Since accounts payable 
do not affect an appropriation, R300 is used.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> "5032 - Acquisition of travel advance" is used since the object classification identifies 
the nature of the transaction (i.e. to provide a travel advance). Once the claim for reimbursement has been processed the 
advance will be reclassified to the appropriate object that identifies the type of goods or services acquired. "6299-Net 
Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" is used to establish or increase an accounts payable.</p><p>2a) The employee submits his claim for settlement. The expenses claimed amount to $1,107.10<br></br>
(including GST of $72.43).</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Operating expenses</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,034.67</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0201</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR GST refundable advance</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>72.43</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13392</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>G111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8171</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accountable advances</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,000.00</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13314</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5032</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>107.10</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Rationale:</strong> The actual operating expenses must be recorded for the period. The accountable advance 
is no longer outstanding, so it is reversed. Since the department owes the individual the balance of $107.10, the amount 
must be accrued and recorded as a payable. Since the employee paid GST on his purchases, this amount should be record the 
GST refundable advance account. Any PST paid would be included as part of the operating expenses.</p><p><strong>Authority Rationale:</strong> In this case, the operating expenses are greater than the accountable advance given 
to the individual. This difference must be charged to the appropriate vote or other authority code e.g. SPAs. This can be 
achieved by netting operating expenses and accountable advances, and coding both with the same vote either B11A or B12A 
(depending on the department's vote structure). If the expense is to be charged to another authority code e.g. SPA, then 
the appropriation must be credited for the full advance and the full expense charged to the other authority. Since GST is 
not to be charged to a departmental appropriation, it is set up as an advance under a special authority G111.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> "0201-Travel -public servants " is used since operating expenses in this Scenario 
relate to travel for public servants. However, other economic objects under reporting object "020" could be used depending 
on the nature of the item. "5032- Acquisition of travel advances" is used to reflect the settlement of the travel advance. 
"6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" is used to establish or increase an accounts payable. Since 
there is GST on the purchases, the GST must be reflected by using "8171 - Payment of GST on purchases".</p><p>2b) Expenses amount to $937.89 (including $61.36 of GST). The employee submits his claim for settlement along with a 
cheque for the amount owing.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Operating expenses</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>876.53</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0201</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR GST refundable advance</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>61.36</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13392</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>G111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8171</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Cash in Hands of Dept. awaiting deposit to RG</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>62.11</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11125</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accountable advances</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,000.00</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13314</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5032</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Rationale:</strong> Operating expenses - see journal entry Scenario B 2a) above.</p><p>Since the individual spent less than the $1,000 (accountable advance), an amount of $62.11 is collected from the employee.</p><p><strong>Authority Rationale:</strong> Since the amount of the advance was previously charged to departmental appropriations, 
there is a requirement to reduce the net charge to the appropriations. To achieve this effect on authorities both the debit 
and credit should be to the same code. In this case, it is suggested that the authority code originally used for the advance 
i.e. B11A or B12A be used. Cash in Hands of Dept awaiting deposit to RG does not effect appropriations, therefore "R300 
- All other assets or liabilities" is used.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> 0201-Travel -public servants " is used since operating expenses in this Scenario relate 
to travel for public servants. However, other economic objects under reporting object "020" could be used depending on the 
nature of the travel or relocation. To record the net impact on Cash Accounts, 5299 would be used. "5032 - Acquisition and 
settlement of travel advances" is used to the settlement of the travel advance.</p><p>2c) The advance is still outstanding at year-end but the travel has been completed.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Operating expenses</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F116</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0201</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accrued liability</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21113</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>Note: all claims where the travel has been completed by 31 March should be settled and accounted for prior to the preparation 
  of the annual financial statements. However, in situations where this has not occurred, departments should record the 
  expenses in the proper year depending on materiality.</p></div><p><strong>FRA Rationale:</strong> Since the advance is outstanding and the exact amount of the settlement is not known, 
an accrued liability is established for the estimated amount. This entry will be reversed in the New Year.</p><p><strong>Authority Rationale:</strong> Since the accountable advance was already charged against the applicable appropriation 
when it was given, no additional charge to an appropriation should be recorded to avoid a double charge. As a result F116 
is used, (an F code has no affect on appropriations). Accrued liabilities do not affect appropriations so R300 is used.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale: "</strong>0201 - Travel/public servants" is used since these operating expenses relate directly 
to expenses incurred by a departmental employee for government travel purposes. However, other economic objects under reporting 
object "020" could be used depending on the nature of the item. "6299 - Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" 
is used to show an increase in accrued liabilities.</p><p>2d) The advance is still outstanding at year-end since the travel will not be completed until the New Year.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Accountable advances</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13314</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>H182</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5049/5032</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accountable advances</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13314</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5049/5032</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>Note: The amount to be reflected in this entry should only be for the advances whereby the travel is to occur in the 
  new year or straddles over two years. The purpose of the transaction is solely for authority purposes i.e. to ensure that 
  the carry-over of any advances is charged to the correct authority at year-end. This entry would only be made in the department's 
  books and no interdepartmental settlements (IS) would be sent to (or be recoverable from) PWGSC.</p></div><p><strong>FRA rationale:</strong> There is no effect from an accrual accounting perspective. Therefore, a debit and credit 
is made to the same account for same amount.</p><p><strong>Authority Rationale:</strong> Since the amount of the advance is still outstanding at year-end, the amount should 
not be charged to the operating or program vote B11A/B12A of the department in that year. Consequently, it must be removed 
and moved to a special authority, H182 - "Payments for accountable temporary advances (e.g. trip advances at year-end)". 
It should only reflect the advances paid out in the old year for travel to be completed in the New Year. It is to be reversed 
in the new year.</p><p><strong>Object rationale:</strong> There is no effect on objects. Therefore the same object is debited and credited for 
the same amount. In this case either "5049- Other adjustments to advances" or "5032 - Acquisition and settlement of travel 
advances" may be used.</p><p>3) The advance carried over in journal entry 2c) must be reversed in the new fiscal year.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Accrued liability</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21113</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Operating expenses</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F116</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0201</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>Note: The purpose of this entry is to remove the accrued liability from the books in the new year since the subsequent 
  settlement of the claim will discharge the liability. When the claim is settled, either entry 2(a) or 2(b), as applicable, 
  will be made.</p></div><p><strong>FRA rationale:</strong> This is a straight reversal of entry 2c) and therefore the same FRAs are used.</p><p><strong>Authority rationale:</strong> There is no impact on appropriations or authority since the appropriations were 
charged in the previous year when the advance was given.</p><p><strong>Object rationale:</strong> The purpose of this entry from an object perspective is to reverse the entry made 
in the old year, as per 2c). To record the net impact on Other Liabilities, "6299 - Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability 
Accounts" is used.</p><p>4) The advance carried over in journal entry 2d) must be reversed in the new fiscal year.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Accountable advances</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13314</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5049</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accountable advances</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13314</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F116</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5049</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA rationale:</strong> Since the Accountable advance account would have been rolled over automatically as part 
of the opening balances, this entry must reflect a Nil effect. Consequently, the debit and credit are to the same account 
for the same amount.</p><p><strong>Authority rationale:</strong> The purpose of this entry is to charge the departmental program (B11A) or operating 
(B12A) vote since this advance should be settled in the current year. Although "H182" was used to record the advance in 
the old year, it should not be used in the new year entry. Instead, the credit is to "F116" since these advances will be 
accounted for at a later date when the claim is submitted for reimbursement.</p><p><strong>Object rationale:</strong> There is no effect on objects. However, adjustments to advances which are neither 
the issuance nor the settlement of advances are recorded against 5049 "Other adjustments to advances".</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement Presentation and Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>Standing advances and temporary advances are recorded in the government's chart of accounts as "Standing advances to 
employees" or "Accountable advances (temporary advances)". They are recorded on the departmental Statement of Financial 
Position as part of financial assets and may be combined for presentation purposes.</p><h4>3.2.4 Debt Deletions</h4><h4>Introduction</h4><p>Debt write-off involves deleting uncollectible debts owing to the Crown but not extinguishing the legal right of the 
Crown to collect the debts. The purpose of write-offs is to reduce the costs of maintaining records of accounts receivable 
that are valueless or uncollectible. Forgiveness and remission is a process that extinguishes a debt, releases the debtor 
from all liability, waives the Crown's right to reinstate the debt, and permits both the Crown and the debtor to remove 
the debt form their accounts. The major difference between the two is that forgiveness is used for non-budgetary transactions 
such as loans whereas remission is applied to budgetary expenditures only.</p><p>No write-off or forgiveness of a debt can occur without an appropriate authority.</p><ul><li>If a debt results from a <strong>budgetary expenditure</strong> (i.e. accounts receivable, repayable contribution) 
  then the debt can be written off under <strong>departmental authority</strong>.</li><li>If a debt results from a <strong>non-budgetary expenditure</strong> (i.e. loan receivable) then the write-off and 
  forgiveness of the debt requires a <strong>charge to a budgetary vote</strong> and <strong>parliamentary authority.</strong></li></ul><p>There are two Scenario s with respect to debt deletions, those that do not require a charge to an appropriation and those 
that do.</p><p><strong>No charge to a Budgetary Vote Required for Write-Off of Debt</strong></p><div class="indent1"><p>1a) A trade accounts receivable is the result of the provision of goods/services. Since the expenditures related to the 
products that were sold were originally charged to a budgetary vote (operating, program, capital vote etc), there is no 
requirement to get it off the books via a budgetary vote.</p><p>1b) Repayable contributions are charged via a budgetary vote (Grant and Contributions appropriation)when payment is made 
to the recipient. To write it off, section 25.1 of the FAA would apply. A charge to an appropriation is not required thus 
an F code would be used, but ministerial approval would be required.</p></div><p>Anything charged to a budgetary vote can be written off under ministerial authority except those debts identified in 
Section 5 of the Debt Write-off regulations. In these cases approval of TB is required but no charge to budgetary vote is 
required.</p><p><strong>Charge to a Budgetary Vote Required for Write-Off of Debt</strong></p><div class="indent1"><p>2a) If the receivable to be deleted is recorded on the Statement of Financial Position through a Loan Vote (originally 
charged to a non-budgetary L vote i.e. a loan or an accountable advance), then departments must charge the write-off to 
a budgetary vote.</p></div><p>For those departments that issue advances through there own Working Capital Advance Appropriations such as DND and DFAIT, 
the accountable advance would have arisen as a result of the original transaction having been charged to a non-budgetary 
vote. For example an individual submits a travel claim for an amount, which is less than the amount advanced, which was 
charged to an accountable advance account (an asset account). If the amount was not collected on the settlement of the claim 
there is amount owing by the claimant which should be set up in departmental books as an accounts receivable. In order to 
write this amount off, the approval of TBS would be required as well as a charge to an appropriation. This is because the 
payment for which recovery is being suspended has never been charged a budgetary vote. It should be noted that since this 
Scenario is only relevant to a few departments this will not be explored in any further detail.</p><p>Generally speaking:</p><p><strong>Non-Budgetary votes</strong> are those for expenditures that are to be recorded on the Statement of Assets/Liabilities 
of the Government of Canada as some kind of asset and are identified by the letter L in the Estimates. Examples include 
loans, accountable advances and investments in Crown Corporations.</p><p><strong>Budgetary Votes</strong> are those for expenditures which are charged to either a program vote, operating vote, 
capital vote or grants &amp; contribution (G&amp;C) vote.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li>Debt Write-off Regulations, 1994 (pursuant to section 25(1) for the FAA)</li><li>FAA act, sections 23, 24 and 25</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Write off of an Accounts Receivable</h4><p>See the Accounts Receivable section of the manual.</p><h4>Scenario B - Write-off of a Conditional Repayable Contribution</h4><p>Same as a write-off for an Account Receivable. See Accounts Receivable section of the manual.</p><h4>Scenario C - Write-off of a Loan Receivable</h4><p>See the Loans Receivable - General section of the manual</p><h4>Scenario D - Write-off of an Unconditional Repayable Contribution</h4><p>See the Unconditional Repayable Contributions section of the manual.</p></section><section anchor="3.3" title="3.3 Inventories"><h4>Introduction</h4><p>Two types of inventories are used by departments:</p><p>1<em>- Consumable Inventories</em> are items of tangible property that are to be consumed in a future year directly or 
indirectly in the delivery of program outputs. They include all items such as equipment, spare parts and material that are 
held in stores and warehouses for issue at a later date to be used in future program delivery. They also include inventories 
held for resale within the Government of Canada. Consumable inventories exclude purchases that meet the capitalization criteria 
specified in TBAS 3.1 Capital Assets.</p><p>2<em>- Inventories held for resale</em> are physical items that will be sold (or used to produce a product which will 
be sold, e.g. raw materials) in the future in the ordinary course of business to parties outside of the Government reporting 
entity.</p><p>The majority of departments will have consumable inventories. There may be some revolving funds and a handful of departments 
that have inventories for resale.</p><h4>Determining Inventory Quantities</h4><p>The physical quantities in inventory may be determined by means of a periodic inventory system or a perpetual inventory 
system.</p><p><strong>(a) Periodic Inventory System</strong></p><p>An actual physical count of goods on hand is taken at the end of each period for which financial statements are to be 
prepared. The goods are counted, weighed or measured, then extended at <em>unit costs</em> to derive the inventory valuation. 
When a periodic inventory system is used, end-of-the period entries are required for (a) transferring opening inventory 
to expense and (b) recording the ending inventory.</p><p>For inventories held for resale, where the inventory records are maintained on a periodic inventory system, typically 
a purchases accounting is used to record acquisition. The balance in the inventory account (which represents the beginning 
inventory) is unchanged during the period. At the end of the accounting period a closing entry is made that debits the Inventory 
account for the ending inventory amount and credits the Inventory account for the beginning inventory amount. Cost of goods 
sold is determined by using the following calculation: Beginning Inventory + Net Purchases - Ending Inventory.</p><p>For consumable inventories, acquisitions of inventory throughout the year may be charged to an expense account. At the 
end of the year, the ending inventory would be recorded with an equivalent reduction in expenses.</p><p>It would not be practical for departments with sizeable inventories to do a physical count every year for the purpose 
of determining ending inventory. Where amounts are significant, central agencies need to know the expenses associated with 
inventory usage more frequently than annually. It is strongly recommended that departments maintain their records on a perpetual 
inventory system (see below)</p><p><strong>(b) Perpetual Inventory System</strong></p><p>It is particularly useful (a) to control and safeguard inventory and (b) to facilitate preparation of monthly statements. 
Furthermore, it is considered to be one of the essential characteristics of a good cost accounting system.</p><p>Purchases are debited directly to the inventory control account and concurrently entered into the detailed inventory 
records. As items of inventory are issued, the transaction is recorded in the accounts so that it carries a perpetual or 
continuing balance of the goods that should be on hand at each date.</p><p>Physical counts are usually made at least annually or on a continuous rotation basis (using sampling) when large inventories 
are involved to verify if there is any loss or error in the record keeping.</p><h4>Discrepancies in Inventory Count</h4><p>Regardless of the inventory control and records in place, loss and errors are always present. When a difference exists 
between the count and the perpetual inventory account balance, an entry is needed for reconciliation.</p><p>Note that in the periodic inventory system, the Inventory Over and Short account does not exist because there are no 
accounting records available against which to compare the physical count. Consequently, overages and shortages are buried 
in cost of goods sold (for inventories held for resale) or operating expenses (for consumable inventories).</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li>TBAS 3.4 Inventories</li><li>CICA Handbook Sections 1520.04, 3030.05-.06, 3030.09-.10</li><li>PS 1500-47, 1500.49</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Purchasing and Issuing Inventory Under a Perpetual Inventory System</h4><p>Department purchases spare parts for vehicles for $50,000. Freight charges of $500 are included on the invoice. Assuming 
the Department uses a perpetual system, purchases &amp; issues are recorded directly in the inventory account as they occur.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record the purchase of inventories</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Inventories held for consumption</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>15110</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A*</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1267</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Inventories held for consumption</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>15110</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A*</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0210</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR GST Refundable Advance Account</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3,535</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13392</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>G111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8171</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>54,035</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>See the Accounts Payable section of the manual to see related entries required for the settlement of the accounts payable. 
See the GST/HST section of the manual to see related entries required for the settlement of the GST.</p></div><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> The purchase of consumable inventories is recorded as a debit to Inventories -Consumables. 
Delivery cost should be capitalized as part of the cost of the inventories. At this point the Department is being charged 
GST on the purchase of inventories, and must pay it. However, the Department will eventually recover this amount from Canada 
Customer and Revenue Agency (CCRA) and should record it as "13392 GST/HST Refundable advance accounts". The cost of the 
consumable inventories plus 7% GST would be set up as an accounts payable in the period since costs were incurred but not 
yet paid. Note: if the inventory had been held for resale, FRA "15120 - Inventories held for resale" would be used instead 
of 15110.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> B11/B12* Since this is a legitimate charge against an operating appropriation, 
it would be recorded against either B11A or B12A depending on whether the department has a program vote (B11A) or an operating 
vote (B12A). Please note that if the entity is a revolving fund the charge to the appropriation would be to A5XX. Since 
GST is not to be charged to a departmental appropriation, it is set up as an advance under a special authority, G111. There 
is no impact on authorities for the accounts payable so the code to be used would be "R300-All other assets and liabilities"</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> Object 1267 is used in this example since spare parts were purchased for the 
Department's vehicles. The appropriate object is used depending on the nature of the purchase. "0210 - Transportation of 
things not elsewhere specified" is used to record the freight charges. If a department's system cannot handle the use of 
more than one object code per asset, the freight charges may be charged to the same code as the asset. Since there is GST/HST 
payable, the GST must be reflected by using, "8171 - Payment of GST on purchases". " 6299 - Accounts Payable/Accrued Charges" 
is used to establish the accrual of the amount owing.</p><p>2) To record inventory issuances of $10,000 from inventory</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Operating Expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>10,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F112</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3452</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Inventories held for consumption</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>10,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>15110</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F312</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3452</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> The charge to 51321 - "Operating Expense" reflects the consumption of inventories 
used for program delivery and the reduction of 15110 - "Inventories held for consumption" is required to remove the items 
that have been consumed. Note if the inventory had been held for resale, the appropriate FRA would be "15210 - Inventories 
for resale" for the credit entry and "51324 - Cost of goods sold" for the debit entry.</p><p><strong>Authority rationale:</strong> There is no impact on the authorities with respect to issuance of inventory since 
the appropriations was charged when the inventory was purchased in journal entry 1). Therefore, F codes are used in this 
transaction. "F112 - Inventory charged to program expenses" would be used for operating expenses. "F312 - reductions from 
(increases to) inventory balances" is used for the inventory account.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> There is no impact on the objects with respect to the issuance of inventory 
since the objects were impacted at the time inventory was purchased in Journal entry 1). "3452 - Usage of inventory" is 
used on both sides of the entry.</p><h4>Scenario B - Purchasing and Issuing Inventory Under a Periodic Inventory System</h4><p>Department purchases spare parts for vehicles for $50,000. Freight charges of $500 are included on the invoice. Assuming 
the Department uses a periodic system, purchases &amp; issues are recorded directly in the inventory account as they occur.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1a) To record the purchase of consumable inventories</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Operating Expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A*</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1267</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Operating Expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A*</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0210</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR GST Refundable Advance Account</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3,535</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13392</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>G111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8171</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>54,035</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>See the Accounts Payable section of the manual to see related entries required for the settlement of the accounts payable. 
See the GST/HST section of the manual to see related entries required for the settlement of the GST.</p></div><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> The purchase of consumable inventories is recorded as a debit to operating expenses. 
Alternatively, the inventories account (FRA 15110) could be debited to record the purchase of inventories.</p><p><strong>Authority rationale:</strong> Same as Scenario A, entry 1).</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> Same as Scenario A, entry 1).</p><p>1b) To record the purchase of inventories held for resale</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Cost of goods sold</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51325</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A*</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1267</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Cost of goods sold</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51325</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A*</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0210</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR GST Refundable Advance Account</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3,535</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13392</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>G111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8171</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>54,035</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> The purchase of inventories held for resale is recorded as a debit to cost of 
goods sold. Alternatively, the inventories account (FRA 15210) could be debited to record the purchase of inventory.</p><p><strong>Authority rationale:</strong> Same as entry 1a).</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> Same as entry 1a).</p>
2) To record the issuance of inventories <p>No entry performed.</p><p>3a) To adjust consumable inventory balance after an inventory count; inventory balance determined to be $5,000 (assume 
opening balance was $2,000)</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Inventories held for consumption</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>15110</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F312</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3452</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Operating Expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F112</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3452</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Inventories held for consumption</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>2,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>15110</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F312</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3452</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> The ending balance of inventory is recorded as an asset while the opening balance 
is removed (alternatively entry could be done on a net basis). The operating expense is reduced to reflect inventory items 
previously expensed but not actually consumed. In the case where purchases of inventory were recorded to the inventory account 
(FRA 15110) instead of operating expense, the same FRAs would be used but the direction of the transactions would change. 
The inventory account would be credited and the operating expense debited to reflect the inventories consumed during the 
period.</p><p><strong>Authority rationale:</strong> Same as Scenario A, entry 2).</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> Same as Scenario A, entry 2).</p><p>3b) To adjust inventory held for resale balance after an inventory count; inventory balance determined to be $5,000 (assuming 
opening inventory balance $2,000)</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Inventories held for resale</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>15210</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F312</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3452</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Cost of goods sold</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51325</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F112</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3452</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Inventories held for resale</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>2,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>15210</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F312</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3452</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA rationale:</strong> The ending balance of inventory is recorded as an asset while the opening balance is 
removed (alternatively entry could be done on a net basis). The cost of goods sold is reduced to reflect inventory items 
previously expensed but not actually sold. In the case where purchases of inventory were recorded to the inventory account 
(FRA 15210) instead of cost of goods sold, the same FRAs would be used but the direction of the transactions would change. 
The inventory account would be credited and the cost of goods sold debited to reflect the inventories sold during the period.</p><p><strong>Authority rationale:</strong> Same as Scenario A, entry 2).</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> Same as Scenario A, entry 2).</p><h4>Scenario C - Inventory Count is lower than records indicate - Write-off required</h4><p>A department performs a physical count of its inventory under a perpetual inventory system and determines that there 
are fewer inventory items present than there should be according to the records. In this case the department must write 
off the portion of the inventory that is no longer available to it. Note that shortages would not be detected under a periodic 
inventory system as a current record of the inventory balance is not maintained. Any lost inventory would be charged to 
cost of goods sold (for inventories for resale) or operating expense (for consumable inventories) as part of the year-end 
adjustment to record the ending inventory balance.</p><p>A physical count determined that the count was lower than the perpetual inventory records balance by $1,000.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record the write-off</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Losses on write-offs and write-downs</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51733</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F112</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3452</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Inventories held for consumption</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>15110</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F312</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3452</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Since there were fewer items found as a result of the inventory count, a loss 
(expense) will result. When a discrepancy is found between the inventory count and inventory records, the perpetual inventory 
records must be adjusted for the shortages (loss). If the inventory had been held for resale, the appropriate FRA would 
be 15210.</p><p><strong>Authority rationale:</strong> This is strictly and accrual accounting entry, there is no impact on authorities, 
therefore F codes are used.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> This is strictly and accrual accounting entry, there is no impact on objects, 
therefore 3452 is used on both sides of the transaction.</p><h4>Scenario D - Inventory Count is higher than records indicate - Record Overage</h4><p>When the department performs a physical count of its inventory, occasionally there is more inventory present than there 
should have been according to the Perpetual Inventory account balance. Such overages are usually the result of a record 
keeping error. Note that overages would not be detected under a periodic inventory system as a current record of the inventory 
balance is not maintained. Any excess inventory would be result in a reduction to cost of goods sold (for inventories for 
resale) or operating expense (for consumable inventories) as part of the year-end adjustment to record the ending inventory 
balance.</p><p>A physical count determined that the count was higher than the perpetual inventory account balance by $800.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record the overage</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Inventories held for consumption</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>800</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>15110</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F312</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3452</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Operating expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>800</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F112</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3452</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Since there were more items found as a result of the inventory count, a reduction 
in operating expenses would be recorded. The perpetual inventory records must be increased to reflect the overage. If the 
inventory had been held for resale, the debit entry would be to FRA "15210 - inventories held for resale" with the credit 
entry to FRA "51325 - Cost of goods sold".</p><p><strong>Authority rationale:</strong> This is strictly and accrual accounting entry, there is no impact on authorities, 
therefore F codes are used.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> This is strictly and accrual accounting entry, there is no impact on objects, 
therefore 3452 is used on both sides of the entry.</p><h4>Scenario E - Inventory Obsolescence - Write-off required</h4><p>A physical count determined that the items worth $2,000 were obsolete.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record inventory obsolescence for both periodic and perpetual inventory systems</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Losses on write-offs and write-downs</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>2,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51733</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F112</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3452</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Inventories - consumable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>2,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>15110</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F312</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3452</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> When inventory is determined to be obsolete, it should be written off. To record 
inventory obsolescence, the inventories account must be reduced by the dollar amount of the obsolescence and a loss recorded. 
If the inventory was held for resale, the credit entry would be to FRA 15210.</p><p><strong>Authority rationale:</strong> This is strictly and accrual accounting entry, there is no impact on authorities, 
therefore F codes are used.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> This is strictly and accrual accounting entry, there is no impact on objects, 
therefore 3452 is used on both sides of the entry.</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement Presentation and Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>Inventories are to be classified as a non-financial asset on the Statement of Financial Position. If a department has 
a significant value of inventories held for resale, it may choose to report these as a financial asset.</p></section><section anchor="3.4" title="3.4 Prepayments (including Prepaids and Deferred Charges)"><h4>Introduction</h4><p><strong>Prepayments</strong></p><p>Prepayments are comprised of contract payments before the receipt of the goods and /or services, advance payments under 
the terms of contribution agreements, prepaid expenses and deferred charges.</p><p><strong>Contract Payments</strong></p><p>Contract advances made prior to the receipt of goods and services shall be charged to expense in the period in which 
all the eligibility criteria have been met or the goods and services received as applicable.</p><p><strong>Advance Payments under Contribution Agreements</strong></p><p>In accordance with the Policy on Transfer Payments, advance payments of the government's share of allowable expenditures 
under a contribution agreement may be made where it is essential to the achievement of the program objectives and is specifically 
provided for in the agreement. As the disbursement is for expenses to be incurred in the future, the payment is recorded 
as a prepayment and is recognized as an expense once the eligible costs have been incurred.</p><p><strong>Prepaid Expenses and Deferred Charges</strong></p><p>A prepaid expense or a deferred charge is an allocation to current and/or future periods of past costs where benefits 
will occur in the current and/or future periods. The distinction between the two is the duration of the benefits to be realized; 
prepaid expenses provide future benefits over a shorter period of time than do deferred charges.</p><p>It should be noted that all research and development costs will be expensed in the period in which they are incurred. 
Costs related to in-house developed software will be accounted for in accordance with the provisions of Treasury Board Accounting 
Standard 3.1.1 on Software and not as a component of research and development costs.</p><p><strong>Amortization</strong></p><p>Government departments have many expenses that they incur on a regular basis. Rent, utilities, subscriptions, payments 
in lieu of taxes and many other expenses must be paid monthly, or on some other cyclical basis. When expenses are prepaid, 
an asset is recognized for the amount paid. This is charged to expenses gradually as the prepaid expense is consumed.</p><p>Where appropriate, amortization of any deferred charge or prepaid expense will be charged as an expense on a systematic 
and rational basis related to use.</p><p><strong>Write-offs</strong></p><p>The balance of any prepaid expense or deferred charge shall be written off to expense in the period that no future benefits 
remain.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li>TBAS 3.3 Prepayments</li><li>TBAS 3.1.1 Software</li><li>CICA 3040, 3070, 3450</li><li>Section 34(b) of the FAA</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Prepaid Expenses</h4><p>A government department rents space in an office building for $25,000 per month. However, the owner of the building demands 
that all tenants of the building prepay at least a year's rent. At the time the department pays the owner the desired amount 
of prepaid rent, there are four months left in the fiscal year.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record the cost of the prepaid rent.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Prepaid Expenses- Rent</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>300,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>14110</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0511</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR GST refundable advance</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13392</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>G111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8171</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>321,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> Since the department paid for a years' rent, it must record an asset for the amount 
that it paid. "14110 - Prepaid Expenses" is used to record the asset. A payable is set up for the amount owing. GST is payable 
on rent (excludes rent paid to PWGSC) or is included as part of rent charges and hence should be recorded to the GST refundable 
advance account.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> It is assumed that the rent expense will be charged to the Operating Vote 
(B12A), but it could also be charged to the Program Vote (B11A) depending on the Department's vote structure. Since Accounts 
Payable does not affect appropriations, R300 is used. Since GST is not to be charged to a departmental appropriation, it 
is set up as an advance under a special authority, G111.</p><p><strong>Object Coding Rationale:</strong> The objects are affected when the transaction is made, so <strong>"</strong>0511 
Rental of office buildings" is used to record the prepaid rent, because the rent is for an office building. "6299 - Net 
Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" is used to establish an account payable for the amount owing. The GST 
must be reflected by using, "8171 - Payment of GST on purchases"</p><p>2) To record the rent consumed by the end of the fiscal year.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Rent Expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F119</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3459/0511</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Prepaid Expenses</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>14110</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F313</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3459/0511</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> At year-end, the department must record an expense equivalent to 4 months of rent 
$100,000 (4 months x $25,000) and reduce the prepaid expense (asset) by an equivalent amount. Please note if the monthly 
rent is material to the operations of the Department the expense could be recorded on a monthly basis. In this case the 
Rent expense would be debited for $25,000 every month with a corresponding credit to Prepaid expenses.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> This is a strictly an accrual transaction, there is no impact on the appropriations. 
Therefore, F codes are used.</p><p><strong>Object Coding Rationale:</strong> This is strictly an accrual transaction with no impact on the objects as they 
are impacted in the previous transaction. Standard object 12 does not impact good, services or transfer payments therefore, 
either "3459 - Amortization of other asset accounts" or "0511 Rental of office buildings" may be used on both sides of the 
entry.</p><h4>Scenario B - Advance Payment under a Contribution Agreement</h4><p>On April 1, the Department makes an advance payment to an individual for research and development in the amount of $50,000. 
The contribution is to cover eligible expenses that will be incurred over the next 4 months.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record the prepayment.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Prepayments of Transfers</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>14120</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B15A/B11A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>2041</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> Since the payment was made in advance of the period for which the eligible costs 
are to be incurred, the payment must be recorded as an asset. A payable is set up for the amount owing.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> In this example, the grant could be charged to either B15A(*) - Grant and 
Contribution vote or B11A - Program Vote. Since Accounts Payable does not affect appropriations, R300 is used.</p><p><strong>Object Coding Rationale:</strong> "2041 Transfer Payments to persons for research and development (incl. Scholarships)". 
"6299 - Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" is used to establish an account payable for the amount owing.</p><p>2) Eligible costs are incurred</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Transfer Payment Expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51119</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F119</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3459/2041</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Prepayments of Transfers</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>14120</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F313</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3459/2041</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> Once the eligibility criteria are met an expense is recorded and the prepayment 
(the asset) is reduced.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> This is strictly an accrual transaction. Since the applicable appropriation 
was previously charged when the payment was made, there is no further effect on appropriations. Consequently, "F" codes 
are used.</p><p><strong>Object Coding Rationale:</strong> This is strictly an accrual transaction with no impact on the objects as they 
are impacted in the previous transaction. Standard object 12 does not impact good, services or transfer payments therefore, 
either "3459-Amortization of other asset accounts" or "2041 Transfer Payments to persons for research and development (incl. 
Scholarships)" is used on both sides of the entry.</p><h4>Alternative Journal Entries</h4><p>Departments may also account for a prepayment by recording the full charge as an expense and then calculating the prepayment 
at each month or year-end.</p><p>1) To record the transfer payment.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Transfer payment expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51119</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B15A/B11A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>2041</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><p>2) To record the prepayment at month-end or year-end</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Prepayments of transfers</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>14120</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F999</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3459/2041</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Transfer payment expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51119</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F999</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3459/2041</p></td></tr></table><p>FRA, Authority and Object coding rationale same as above.</p><h4>Scenario C - Payments made in advance of receiving goods.</h4><p>The Department enters into a contract for goods where by they are required to make a payment in advance of receiving 
those goods in accordance with section 34(b) of the FAA. The amount of the prepayment is $21,400 (including GST).</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record the prepayment.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Prepaid expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>20,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>14110</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A*</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1xxx</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR GST refundable advance</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,400</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13392</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>G111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8171</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21,400</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> Since the department paid for goods in advance, it must record an asset for the 
amount that it paid. "14110-Prepaid Expenses" is used to record the asset. A payable is set up for the amount owing. GST 
is recorded to the GST refundable advance account.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> It is assumed that the prepaid expense will be charged to the Operating 
Vote (B12A), but it could also be charged to the Program Vote (B11A) depending on the Department's vote structure. Since 
Accounts Payable does not affect appropriations, R300 is used. Since GST is not to be charged to a departmental appropriation, 
it is set up as an advance under a special authority, G111.</p><p><strong>Object Coding Rationale:</strong> The objects are affected when the transaction is made, depending on the nature 
of the good the appropriate code would be used. "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" is used to establish 
an account payable for the amount owing. The GST must be reflected by using "8171-Payment of GST on purchases"</p><p>2) Goods are received.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Operating Expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>20,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51119</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F119</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3459</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Prepaid Expenses</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>20,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>14110</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F313</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3459</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> Once the goods are received the department must record an expense $20,000 and 
reduce prepaid expense (asset) by an equivalent amount.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> This is a strictly an accrual transaction. Since the applicable appropriation 
was previously charged when the payment was made, there is no further effect on appropriations. Consequently, "F" codes 
are used.</p><p><strong>Object Coding Rationale:</strong> This is strictly an accrual transaction with no impact on the objects as they 
are impacted in the previous transaction. Standard object 12 does not impact good, services or transfer payments therefore, 
"3459-Amortization of other asset accounts" is used on both sides of the entry.</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement Presentation and Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>Prepaid expenses, deferred charges and prepayments will be reflected on the Statement of Financial Position as non-financial 
assets under the heading Prepayments. Major items should be shown separately. Please note that this in variance with the 
current PS 3410 which records transfer payments in advance as a financial asset.</p></section><section anchor="3.5" title="3.5 Capital Assets"><p>Capital Assets are tangible assets that are purchased, constructed, developed or otherwise acquired and:</p><ol class="lower-alpha"><li>are held for use in the production or supply of goods, the delivery of services or to produce program outputs;</li><li>have a useful life extending beyond one fiscal year and are intended to be used on a continuing basis; and,</li><li>are not intended for resale in the ordinary course of operations.</li></ol><p>For the government, capital assets have the following characteristics:</p><ol class="lower-alpha"><li>beneficial ownership and control clearly rest with the government;</li><li>the asset is used to achieve government objectives; and,</li><li>risks and benefits of ownership clearly rest with the government (as is the case of capital leases).</li></ol><p>For government accounting purposes capital assets generally include all assets treated as capital assets under Public 
Sector Accounting Board recommendations and generally accepted accounting principles in Canada, having an initial cost of 
$10,000 or more. Departments may choose a lower threshold value.</p><p>The cost of property, equipment and other capital assets including betterments is essentially a long-term prepayment 
of an expense in advance of the use of an asset. As the economic service life of the asset expires, the cost of the asset 
is systematically allocated to operations as an expense called "amortization".</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li>TBAS 3.1 Capital Assets</li><li>TBAS 3.1.1 Software</li><li>PS 3150</li><li>CICA 3060</li></ul><h4>3.5.1 Tangible Capital Assets</h4><h4>Introduction</h4><p>Tangible capital assets are a significant economic resource managed by governments and a key component in the delivery 
of many government programs. Tangible capital assets include such diverse items as land, heritage buildings, military assets, 
infrastructure assets, purchased computer software, in-house developed software, computer hardware, assets acquired by capital 
leases or by donations, etc.</p><p><strong>Betterments versus Repairs</strong></p><p>The cost incurred to enhance the service potential of a capital asset is a betterment. Service potential may be enhanced 
when there is an increase in the previously assessed physical output or service capacity, associated operating costs are 
lowered, the useful life is extended, or the quality of output is improved. The cost incurred in the maintenance of the 
service potential of a capital asset is a repair, not a betterment.</p><p><strong>Write-down</strong></p><p>A department would write down the cost of a tangible capital asset when it can demonstrate that the reduction in future 
economic benefits is expected to be permanent. Conditions that may indicate that the future economic benefits associated 
with a tangible capital asset have been reduced and a write-down is appropriate include:</p><ol class="lower-alpha"><li>a change in the extent to which the asset is used;</li><li>a change in the manner in which the asset is used;</li><li>significant technological developments;</li><li>physical damage;</li><li>removal of the asset from service;</li><li>a decline in or cessation of, the need for the services provided by the asset;</li><li>a decision to halt construction of the asset before it is complete or in usable or saleable condition;</li><li>a change in the law or environment affecting the extent to which the asset can be used.</li></ol><p>PS 3150.36</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li>TBAS 3.1 - Capital Assets</li><li>TBAS 3.1.1 - Software</li><li>TBAS 1.2</li><li>CICA 3060</li><li>PS 3150</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Purchase of a Tangible Capital Asset</h4><p>The Department purchased and received a vehicle for $23,500 on January 31, 2000. Delivery costs are an additional $500. 
Total GST is $1,680. Payment does not take place until the following fiscal year, April 15, 2000. The vehicle has a useful 
life of 10 years with no estimated residual value.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>These entries assume the vehicle is charged directly to the asset FRA. See alternative entry if amounts are to be initially
