Equipment</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16222</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F311</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>7061/7099</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5,350</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>See Accounts Payable section for related entries regarding settlement of payable.</p></div><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Since the $5,000 is a component of the total cost of the equipment, it is capitalized. 
Upon expiration of the lease, the amount capitalized as leased equipment is fully amortized and taken off the books (note: 
at this point the lease obligation is fully discharged). Since the equipment has already been amortized for 5 years, the 
accumulated amortization must be recorded on the books. The remaining $5,000 will be amortized over the next two years. 
GST of $350 (7% on $5,000) is owed on the purchase.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> Only $5,000 will get charged to an appropriation since the $100,000 was 
already charged when the lease payments were made over the last 5 years.</p><p>(****) In this example, it is assumed the purchase would be charged to a capital vote- B14A. However, depending on the 
department, the following authority codes could be used: B11A - Program Vote, B12A Operating Vote, and A131 Spending of 
amounts equivalent to proceeds from disposal of surplus Crown assets. There is no affect on appropriations throughout the 
rest of the entry therefore the applicable F codes are used, as well as R300 for the accounts payable set up.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> There is no affect on expenditures in this transaction except for the additional 
$5,000 spent on the Informatics equipment. To capture the accumulated amortization on the equipment 7061 or 7099 is used. 
Economic object 1221 reflects the $5,000 acquisition of the residual Informatics capital asset. "6299-Net Increase or Decrease 
to Other Liability Accounts" is used to establish the payable. To indicate the nil effect on the remainder of the transaction 
"7099-Net Increase or Decrease in Other Transactions.</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement Presentation and Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>The gross amount of assets under capital leases and related accumulated amortization should be disclosed. Obligations 
related to leased assets should be shown separately from other financial obligations. Particulars of obligations related 
to leased assets, including interest rates and expiry dates, should be shown separately in the notes to the financial statements 
from other financial obligations. Significant restrictions imposed on the lessee as a result of the lease agreement should 
be disclosed.</p><p>Disclosure should be made of the future minimum lease payments in aggregate and for each of the five succeeding years. 
A separate deduction should be made from the aggregate figure for amounts included in the minimum lease payments representing 
executory costs and imputed interest. The resultant net amount would be the balance of the unpaid obligation.</p><p>The amount of amortization for leased property should be disclosed separately or as part of amortization and amortization 
expense for fixed assets. Disclosure should be made of methods and rates of amortization.</p><p>Interest expense related to lease obligations should be disclosed separately.</p><h5>3.5.1.2 Assets Under Construction</h5><h4>Introduction</h4><p>The cost of a constructed asset would include direct construction or development costs (such as materials and labour), 
and overhead costs directly attributable to the construction or development activity. PS 3150.12</p><p>Capitalization of costs ceases, however, when a tangible capital asset is ready for use. Determining when a tangible 
capital asset, or a portion thereof, is ready for productive use requires consideration of the circumstances in which it 
is to be operated. Normally it would be predetermined by reference to factors such as productive capacity, occupancy level, 
or the passage of time. PS 3150.17</p><p>Assets under construction also include those assets that have been acquired but require additional work to get them ready 
for use. See Scenario A.</p><p><strong>Amortization</strong></p><p>Assets under construction are not amortized while they are still being constructed. This is because the asset is not 
being used in program delivery. The amortization process starts when the asset's construction is complete and has begun 
being used by the department.</p><ol class="lower-alpha"><li>to which the asset can be used.</li></ol><h4>References</h4><ul><li>PS 3150.12,.17,.36,.45</li><li>TBAS 3.1 Capital Assets</li><li>TBAS 1.2 Departmental and Agency Financial Statements</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Department purchases a computer but work is still required to get it ready for use.</h4><p>Department buys computer hardware for $200,000. The equipment is not functional until it has been installed properly 
and is ready for use. Until that time the equipment will not be amortized. The following costs are associated with getting 
the equipment ready for use.</p><ul><li>Freight $500</li><li>Computer consultants to set up the hardware $35,000</li><li>Departmental Staff salaries used to set up hardware $20,000</li><li>Additional circuits required to modify the hardware to adapt to Departmental needs $5,000</li><li>It is assumed that the department has a separate capital vote.</li></ul><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) Purchase of the computer hardware</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Other WIP - Computer Hardware</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>200,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16319</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B14A(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1226</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR GST Refundable Advance Account</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>14,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13392</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>G111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8171</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>214,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> The asset is over the threshold $10,000 amount and must be capitalized. However, 
since the asset is not ready for use, the costs must be allocated to a work in progress (WIP) account. This is essential 
since the asset should not be amortized. At this point the Department is being charged GST on the computer, and must pay 
it to the vendor. However, as the Department will eventually recover this amount from Canada Customs and Revenue Agency 
(CCRA) they should record it as an asset in "13392 GST/HST Refundable advance accounts". Since the Department has not paid 
for the computer equipment, a payable must be recorded for the amount owing.</p><p>Note: if the department's system cannot accommodate this entry, the purchase of hardware may first be charged to operating 
expenses and then transferred to the work in process account. See Section 3.5.1 Capital Assets, Scenario C, journal entries 
1 and 2 for an example of this type of entry.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> (*) In this example it is assumed this purchase would be charged to the 
capital vote. However, depending on the department's vote structure and the asset purchased, the following authority codes 
could be used: B11A - Program Vote or B12A Operating Vote. Since GST is not to be charged to a departmental appropriation, 
it is set up as an advance under a special authority, G111. Since Accounts Payable has no impact on the authority side, 
"R300 - All Other Assets and Liabilities" is used.</p><p><strong>Object Coding Rationale:</strong> "1226 - Computer Equipment - Large/medium- mainframe, mini" would be used to 
reflect the purchase of this equipment. Since there is GST/HST payable, the GST must be reflected by using, "8171-Payment 
of GST on purchases". "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" is used to establish the accrual of the 
amount owing.</p><p>2) Departmental salaries are paid and a portion is allocated to the WIP account</p><div class="indent1"><p>2a) Departmental Salaries and wages are paid</p></div><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Salaries and wages Expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51311</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0101</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Payroll Control Account 100,000</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>63DDD</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight">
 </td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> Salaries and wages for employees in the department are recorded as an operating 
expense and the amount is paid through the Payroll Control Account. The amount that pertains to the asset in question will 
get allocated to the Computer equipment WIP account accordingly (see below).</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> Salaries can be charged to of the Department's capital, program or operating 
appropriation depending on the vote structure of the Department. Payroll Control account has no impact on appropriations 
and is therefore coded as 0000.</p><p><strong>Object Coding Rationale:</strong> "0101- Civilian regular time - continuing employment" is used for salaries 
paid to full-time indeterminate employees. All RG interface Control Accounts are zero filled (0000), with the exception 
of I/S Control Accounts, at the object level.</p><div class="indent1"><p>2b) Salaries related to the computer equipment ($20,000) are charged to the WIP account</p></div><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Other WIP - Computer Hardware</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>20,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16319</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B14A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3425</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Salaries and wages Expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>20,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51311</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3717</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> $20,000 of salaries and wages that relate directly to the computer hardware will 
get re-allocated from operating expenses to the computer equipment WIP account.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> The salaries and wages should be re-allocated from the program or operating 
vote to the capital vote.</p><p><strong>Object Coding Rationale:</strong> Since the salaries are being reallocated to a WIP account within the same department 
"3425 - Reallocation of expenditures/costs within a department" is used for the debit side of the transaction and "3717 
- Recoveries of expenditures/costs within a department" is used on the credit side of the transaction. Since both of these 
items relate to standard object 12 they will be netted against each other, therefore having a nil effect.</p><p>3) To record additional expenses related to the computer hardware</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Other WIP - Computer Hardware (Consulting)</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>35,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16319</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B14A(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0472</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Other WIP - Computer Hardware (Freight)</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16319</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B14A(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0210</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Other WIP - Computer Hardware (Circuits)</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16319</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B14A(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1229</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR GST refundable advance</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>2,485</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13392</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>G111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8171</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>42,985</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> Once again the asset is still not ready for use, invoices has been received for 
consulting fees, additional circuits and freight so these amounts must be capitalized to the computer hardware WIP account. 
As well, a liability must be set up for the amount owing to the contractor. In this case, "21111 - Accounts Payable" is 
used.</p><p>Note: if the department's system cannot accommodate this entry, these costs may first be charged to operating expenses 
and then transferred to the work in process account. See Section 3.5.1 Capital Assets, Scenario C, journal entries 1 and 
2 for an example of this type of entry.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> B14A(*) Consulting fees, freight and circuits that pertain to the computer 
is to be paid out of the Department's capital, program or operating appropriation depending the vote structure of the Department. 
Since Accounts Payable has no impact on the authority side, "R300 - All Other Assets and Liabilities" is used</p><p><strong>Object Coding Rationale:</strong> Assuming that the freight charges are billed separately from the computer hardware 
purchase "0210 - Transportation of things not elsewhere specified" is used. "0472 - Information Technology consultants" 
is used for the consulting fees incurred by the department."1229 - Computer Equipment parts" is used for the circuits. "6299 
- Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" is used to establish the accrual of the amount owing.</p><p>4) The computer is ready for use</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Computer Hardware</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>260,500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16122</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F999</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3425</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Other WIP-Computer Hardware</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>260,500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16319</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F999</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3717</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> Since the asset is now ready for use, it also now must start being amortized. 
This means that the balance in WIP must reallocated to the Computer Hardware (asset) account.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> This is strictly an accrual transaction, so there is no impact on the authority 
side. The charge to the appropriation was made in the previous entry. In this case, "F999 - Other F Codes" will be both 
debited and credited, so there will be no effect on the authorities.</p><p><strong>Object Coding Rationale:</strong> Since this is a re-allocation from the WIP account to the asset account within 
the same department, "3425 - Reallocation of expenditures/costs within a department" is used for the debit side of the transaction 
and "3717 - Recoveries of expenditures/costs within a department" is used on the credit side of the transaction. Since both 
of these items relate to standard object 12 they will be netted against each other, therefore having a nil effect.</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement Presentation and Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>The department's Statement of Financial Position should disclose the net book value of tangible capital assets not being 
amortized because they are under construction or development. PS 3150.45.</p></section></chapter><chapter anchor="4" title="4.0 Liabilities"><p>Liabilities are financial obligations to outside organizations and individuals as a result of transactions and events 
on or before the accounting date. They are the result of contracts, agreements and legislation in force at the accounting 
date that require the government to repay borrowings or to pay for goods and services acquired or provided prior to the 
accounting date. PS 1500.39</p><p>Reporting on a government's total liabilities at the accounting date is necessary to ensure a complete reporting of transactions 
and events, and to understand and assess demands on financial resources. PS 1500.40</p><p>Liabilities are presented on the Statement of Financial Position, and include accounts payable and accrued liabilities, 
allowances for employee benefits, deferred revenue etc.</p><section anchor="4.1" title="4.1 Accounts Payable"><h4>Introduction</h4><p>Accounts payable are balances owed to trade creditors, sundry creditors and others for goods, services, loans, transfer 
payments etc. Payables arise because of the time lag between the requirement to record the obligation and the requirement 
to satisfy the obligation at a later date.</p><p>Particular attention must be paid to transactions occurring near the end of one accounting period and at the beginning 
of the next to ascertain that the goods received (the inventory) and the liability (accounts payable) for those goods both 
are recorded in the same period.</p><p>Accrued liabilities should be set up for estimated amounts for goods or services received but not recorded at the end 
of each month, for any material amounts. These should be subsequently reversed when definitive amounts are known, at which 
time an accounts payable would be set up, or at the beginning of the next month depending on a department's system.</p><p>Since Accounts Payable do not affect appropriations, the R300 authority code should always be used.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li>PS 1500.41, 1500.43, 1800.25</li><li>CICA 3860.43-.95 (for disclosure)</li></ul><h4>Scenario A</h4><p>Supplies of $500 are purchased and received.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record purchase of supplies (assume purchase and receipt of goods at same time)</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Operating Expenses</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11XX</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR GST/HST Refundable Advance Account</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>35</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13392</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>G111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8171</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>535</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>For entries related to the settlement of the GST Refundable Advance Account please see the Sales Tax section of the manual.</p></div><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Since supplies were purchased and received in the period, operating expenses must 
be recorded. At this point the Department is being charged GST on the purchase of supplies, and must pay it. However, the 
Department will eventually recover this amount from Canada Customer and Revenue Agency (CCRA) and should record it as "13392 
GST/HST Refundable advance accounts". The cost of the operating expenses plus 7% GST would be accrued as an accounts payable 
in the period since expenses were incurred but not yet paid.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> Since this is a legitimate charge against an operating appropriation, it 
would be recorded against either B11A or B12A depending on whether the department has a program vote (B11A) or an operating 
vote (B12A). Since GST is not to be charged to a departmental appropriation, authority G111 is used. Accounts Payable does 
not affect the appropriations, thus "R300 -Total amounts of all other assets and liabilities" would be used.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> Depending on the actual supplies purchased, the appropriate economic object 
in sub-category 11 should be used. "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" is used to record the establishment 
an accounts payable. Since there has been an acquisition of goods on which GST/HST is payable, the related GST must be reflected 
by using, "8171 - Payment of GST on purchases"</p><p>2) Department requisitions Receiver General (RG) for payment.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>535</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Payments in Transit</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>535</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11134</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5299</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Since the payment is being requisitioned, the payable is reversed and the Payment 
in Transit account would reflect these payments requisitioned but not yet paid. The control account should not be charged 
until PWGSC has confirmed that the payment has been made.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> Neither of the accounts impacts appropriations so both sides of the entry 
must therefore be coded to R300-Total amounts of all other assets and liabilities.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" are used to indicate 
a settlement of accounts payable. To record the net impact on Cash Accounts, 5299 would be used.</p><p>3) The Receiver General (RG) notifies the department that the payment is made at which time the Department will make 
the following entry:</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Payments in Transit</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>535</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11134</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Cash Payment Control Account</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>535</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>61DDD</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0000</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Once the payment is made, Payments in Transit is reversed and the Cash Payment 
Control account is credited to reflect that the RG has made the payment. The last three digits of the control account will 
be the department number.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> Neither of these accounts affect appropriations. The authority code is 0000 
for the "Cash Payment Control Account" and "R300-All other assets and liabilities" for Payments in Transit.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> To record the net impact on Cash Accounts, 5299 would be used. All RG interface 
Control Accounts are zero filled (0000), with the exception of I/S Control Accounts, at the object level.</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement Presentation and Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>Accounts payable are to be classified as a liability in the Statement of Financial Position.</p></section><section anchor="4.2" title="4.2 Deferred Revenues"><h4>Introduction</h4><p>Deferred revenues or unearned revenues are monies received in advance from parties external to government for which a 
government entity will provide specified goods or services in the near future. Deferred revenues related to unspecified 
goods and services are recorded in specified purpose accounts (see Specified Purpose Accounts section of this manual).</p><p>The unearned revenues may arise from the following types of sales of goods and services to outside parties:</p><ul><li>Rights and privileges;</li><li>Lease and Use of Public Property;</li><li>Services of a regulatory nature;</li><li>Services of a non-regulatory nature;</li><li>Sales of goods and information products;</li><li>Other fees and charges; etc.</li></ul><p>For government accounting purposes, the revenue recognition principle dictates that revenue is recorded in the period 
it is realized. When revenues are received prior to being realized, the amount applicable to future periods is deferred 
to those future periods.</p><p>The amount unearned or deferred (received in advance of realisation) is considered a liability because it represents 
an obligation arising from a past transaction to provide a good or service in the future.</p><p>As the goods are provided or the services are rendered the government entity will realize and recognize its revenue in 
the appropriate accounting period.</p><p>The following transactions deal with the " normal day to day situations" with respect to external non-tax revenues. More 
complex transactions that deal with specified purpose accounts can be found in the section entitled "Specified Purpose Accounts" 
of the manual.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li>CICA 1510.05, 1510.07, 3400</li><li>PS 1500.34, 1800.25, 1800.40, 3100.07-.12, 3410.47-.48</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Non Respendable Revenue</h4><p>The Department receives $100 in year 1 for services that will not be performed until year 2.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record the fee of $100 collected in Year 1.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Cash in the hands of the Departments awaiting deposit to the RG</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11125</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Deferred revenues</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21510</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>D/E(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>45xx</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Rationale:</strong> The Department must recognize the monies received in advance from the outside party in 
the appropriate cash account. Since the fees relate to revenue that will be realized in a subsequent period, the Department 
must recognize this fee as other deferred revenue (a liability account).</p><p><strong>Authority Rationale:</strong> There is no impact on the authority side for cash. Therefore R300 would be used. 
D/E(*) Depending on which type of revenue is considered in the scenario, the Department would choose the appropriate code 
from the following chart.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p><strong>Statutory Non-Tax Revenue</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p><strong>Non Statutory Non-Tax Revenue</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p><strong>Non-Respendable Revenue</strong></p></th><td class="alignTopCenter"><p>D221 to D223</p></td><td class="alignTopCenter"><p>E221 to E223</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> To record the net impact on Cash Accounts, 5299 would be used. Economic objects are 
recorded on a cash receipt basis for deferred revenues. Depending on the type of revenue received, the appropriate economic 
object within the 45xx category would be used.</p><p>2) The Department performs the required service or provides the required goods for the outside party</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Deferred revenues</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21510</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>D/E(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4888</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Non tax revenue</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4231x</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>D/E(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4888</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Rationale:</strong> As revenue is earned by performing the required service or providing the good, the appropriate 
amount is brought into revenue. At this point it is permissible for the Department to recognize revenue. At the same time 
the equivalent amount will be removed from the liability account for the deferred revenue (21510).</p><p><strong>Authority Rationale:</strong> This is strictly an accrual transaction. Authorities are not affected here at all. 
However, the system requires that authority codes be input. In order to achieve a nil effect on departmental authorities 
one option would be to debit and credit the same authority for the same amount. D/E(*) Depending on which type of revenue 
is considered in the Scenario , the department would choose the appropriate code from the following chart. Note: if E221 
was the applicable code then it would be used on both the credit and debit side of the entry.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p><strong>Statutory Non-Tax Revenue</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p><strong>Non Statutory Non-Tax Revenue</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p><strong>Non-Respendable Revenue</strong></p></th><td class="alignTopCenter"><p>D221 to D223</p></td><td class="alignTopCenter"><p>E221 to E223</p></td></tr></table><p>Another option would be use R300 for Other Deferred revenues and F259 for non- tax revenue. Both the R300 and F259 have 
no effect on appropriations thereby producing the same results as the above option.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale: "</strong>4888 - reallocation from non budgetary funds and accounts" must be used here since 
this is a reallocation of deferred revenue to non-tax revenue. There is no effect on the economic object at this point. 
The economic object captured the revenue in the previous journal entry.</p><h4>Scenario B - Respendable Revenue</h4><p>The Department receives $100 in year 1 for services that will not be performed until year 2.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record the fee of $100 collected in Year 1 and record revenue credited to the vote (done at the same time).</p><p>1a) To record the fee of $100 collected in Year 1</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Cash in the hands of the Departments awaiting deposit to the RG</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11125</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Deferred revenues</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21510</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>D/E(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>45xx</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Rationale:</strong> The Department must recognize the monies received in advance from the outside party in 
the appropriate cash account. Since the fees relate to revenue that will be realized in a subsequent period, the Department 
must recognize this fee as deferred revenue (a liability account).</p><p><strong>Authority Rationale:</strong> There is no impact on the authority side for cash, therefore R300 would be used. 
D/E(*) Depending on which type of revenue is considered in the Scenario , the Department would choose the appropriate code 
from the following chart.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p><strong>Statutory Non-Tax Revenue</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p><strong>Non Statutory Non-Tax Revenue</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p><strong>Respendable Revenue</strong></p></th><td class="alignTopCenter"><p>D211 to D213</p></td><td class="alignTopCenter"><p>E211 to E213</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> To record the net impact on Cash Accounts, 5299 would be used. Economic objects are 
recorded on a cash receipt basis for deferred revenues. Depending on the type of revenue received, the appropriate economic 
object within the 45xx category would be used.</p><p>1b) Since the cash is received by the Department, and the Department has the authority to respend it, the revenue is 
credited to the vote</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Deferred revenues</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21510</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>D218/E218</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>7099</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Deferred revenues</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21510</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B13A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>7099</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA rationale:</strong> This is strictly an authority transaction. To ensure there is no effect on FRAs, the 
same FRA is debited and credited for the same amount.</p><p><strong>Authority rationale:</strong> When a Department has authority to re-spend revenue, it can only be re-spent when 
the revenue is actually received (i.e. on a cash basis). Only the revenue portion of the transaction is affected. In this 
case, $100. To reflect this, the cash received is credited to "B13A Revenues credited to the vote". The debit will be to 
either a D218 (statutory) or E218 (non-statutory) depending on the situation It is important that either D218 and E218 be 
used in this transaction and that the authority code used to set up the revenue transaction not be used. Otherwise, the 
revenue charging authority information would be lost.</p><p><strong>Object rationale:</strong> This is strictly an authority transaction. To ensure there is no effect on objects, 
the same object is debited and credited for the same amount. "7099- Net Increase or Decrease in Other Transactions" is used 
here since this will have a nil effect on objects</p><p>2) The Department performs the required service or provides the required goods for the outside party</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Deferred revenues</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21510</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>D/E(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4888</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Non tax revenue</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4231x</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>D/E(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4888</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Rationale:</strong> As revenue is earned by performing the required service or providing the good, the appropriate 
amount is brought into revenue. At this point it is permissible for the Department to recognize revenue. At the same time 
the equivalent amount will be removed from the liability account for the deferred revenue (21510).</p><p><strong>Authority Rationale:</strong> This is strictly an accrual transaction. Authorities are not affected here at all. 
However, the system requires that authority codes be input. In order to achieve a nil effect on departmental authorities 
one option would be to debit and credit the same authority for the same amount. D/E(*) Depending on which type of revenue 
is considered in the Scenario , the department would choose the appropriate code from the following chart. Note: if D211 
was the applicable code then it would be used on both the credit and debit side of the entry.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p><strong>Statutory Non-Tax Revenue</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p><strong>Non Statutory Non-Tax Revenue</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p><strong>Respendable Revenue</strong></p></th><td class="alignTopCenter"><p>D211 to D213</p></td><td class="alignTopCenter"><p>E211 to E213</p></td></tr></table><p>Another option would be use R300 for Other Deferred revenues and F259 for non- tax revenue. Both the R300 and F259 have 
no effect on appropriations thereby producing the same results as the above option.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale: "</strong>4888 - reallocation from non budgetary funds and accounts" must be used here since 
this is a reallocation of deferred revenue to non-tax revenue. There is no effect on the economic object at this point. 
The economic object has captured the revenue in the previous journal entry.</p><h4>Scenario C - Refund</h4><p>The outside party requests a refund prior to the Department performing the required service or providing the required 
goods.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) Same as Scenario A 1)</p><p>2) The outside party requests a refund prior to the Department performing the required service or providing the required 
goods.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Deferred revenues</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21510</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>D/E(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>45xx</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Rationale:</strong> The Department proceeds with the refund of money received in advance from the appropriate 
cash account. Since the revenue was never realized the Department must reduce the Other Deferred Revenue and set up a payable.</p><p><strong>Authority Rationale:</strong> The authority code for the deferred revenue would be debited by the equivalent 
amount since the service or good was not provided. D/E(*) Depending on which type of revenue is considered in the Scenario 
, the department would choose the appropriate code from the following chart.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p><strong>Statutory Non-Tax Revenue</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p><strong>Non Statutory Non-Tax Revenue</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p><strong>Respendable Revenue</strong></p></th><td class="alignTopCenter"><p>D211 to D213</p></td><td class="alignTopCenter"><p>E211 to E213</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p><strong>Non-Respendable Revenue</strong></p></th><td class="alignTopCenter"><p>D221 to D223</p></td><td class="alignTopCenter"><p>E221 to E223</p></td></tr></table><p>Accounts payables do not affect appropriations, the code R300 would be used.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> The same economic object 45xx would be reversed since the payment was refunded. "6299-Net 
Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" is used to establish an accounts payable".</p><p><strong>Please note: If the transaction deals with respendable revenue it would necessary to reverse the entry that is 
described in Scenario B, Journal entry 1b) of this section as well.</strong></p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement Presentation and Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>Deferred Revenue should be recorded under the liability section of the Department's Statement of Financial Position.</p></section><section anchor="4.3" title="4.3 Loan Guarantees"><h4>Introduction</h4><p>A loan guarantee is a promise to pay all or a part of the principal and/or interest on a debt obligation in the event 
of default by the borrower.</p><p><strong>Contingent Liability</strong></p><p>A loan guarantee is a contingent liability of the government. The generally accepted accounting principles for contingent 
liabilities are, therefore, appropriate for loan guarantees. See the Contingencies Section of the Manual.</p><p><strong>To the extent that the future event is likely to occur or fail to occur, and a reasonable estimate of the loss 
can be made, an estimated liability is accrued and an expense recorded on the government consolidated financial statements 
and NOT on the departmental financial statements unless so advised by TBS.</strong></p><p>Departments will only set up a liability (payable) and a corresponding expense once the criteria of the PAYE policy has 
been met.</p><p>Departments will provide information on loan guarantees to Receiver General in accordance with the Public Accounts Instruction 
Manual (PAIM).</p><p><strong>Provision for Losses</strong></p><p>For the time being, TBS will be recording the provision for losses on loan guarantees based on information provided by 
departments to the Receiver General. Please see <strong><a href="/fin/sigs/Information_Bulletins/aatp_info-eng.asp">FY 2001-02 FIS Transition Period -Transition Protocol and Accounting 
Requirements</a></strong> document issued on November 15, 2000.</p><p><strong>Payment of Loan Guarantees</strong></p><p>If the Department has made payments under the terms of a guarantee and has recourse to recover amounts paid from the 
borrower, such amounts should be accounted for in accordance with LOANS RECEIVABLE Section PS 3050. (PS 3310.21). See Loans 
Receivable Section of this manual.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li>PS 3310</li><li>Contingencies Section of the FIS Accounting Manual</li><li>TBAS 1.2 Departmental and Agency Financial Statements</li><li>PS 1500</li><li>Loans Receivable Section of the FIS Accounting Manual</li></ul><p><strong><a href="/fin/sigs/Information_Bulletins/aatp_info-eng.asp">FY 2001-02 FIS Transition Period -Transition Protocol and Accounting Requirements</a></strong> document issued on 
November 15, 2000</p><h4>Scenario A - Department provides loan guarantee.</h4><p>A Department has provided an outside organization for the purpose of development assistance to foreign countries with 
a loan guarantee in year 1. The outside organization defaults on the loan in year 2. The amount of the loan is $100,000.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) Year 1 - Department provides Loan Guarantee</p><p><strong>No journal entry is required</strong>.</p><p>The Department will only disclose by way of a note to the departmental financial statement that they have contingencies 
in the form of loan guarantees. (See TBAS 3.6 Contingencies)</p><p>2a) Year 2 - Borrower defaults and Department pays out loan guarantee to lender</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Expenses related to loan guarantees</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51727</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>A/B(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>2304</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><p>(See section on Accounts Payable for the entries required for settlement of accounts payable)</p><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> When the borrower defaults on the loan the department is required to make the 
payment to the lender and an expense is incurred. The Department must set up a payable for the amount owing. It should be 
noted, that due to system limitations and requirements to charge an appropriation the debit is made to Expenses related 
to loan guarantees instead of a receivable. As a result, the Expenses related to loan guarantee is subsequently removed 
from the books by a credit in journal entry 3) see below.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> A/B(*) Depending on the Department's vote structure the following the payment 
can be charged either B11A(*) - Program Vote, B12A - Operating Vote. If a department has a specific statutory budgetary 
appropriation for this purpose, it may use this appropriation (i.e. Indian and Northern Affairs A852). Since accounts payable 
has no impact on appropriations, R300 is used.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale</strong>: "6299- Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability accounts" should be used to indicate 
the establishment of the accrued payable. "2304- Other payments for development assistance to foreign countries" would be 
used in this case.</p><p>2b) Year 2 - Set up a receivable to record money owed to the corporation by the borrower</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Loans/advances on expired loan guarantees</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13371</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5010</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Expenses related to loan guarantees</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51727</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F154</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>2304</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> Since the Department has made payments under the terms of a guarantee and has 
recourse to recover amounts paid from the borrower, such amounts should be accounted for as a loans receivable. Normally, 
the credit would be an allowance for doubtful loans. However, since departments do not record an allowance (See Loans Receivable 
section of manual), the credit will be to expenses related to loan guarantees.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> There is no impact on appropriations at this stage. R300 is used to reflect 
the receivable and "F154-Expenses related to loan guarantees" is used for the other side of the transaction.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> "5010 - Acquisition of loans with cash" should be used for establishing the loan receivable. 
The economic object debited in entry 2a) would be credited in this entry, in this case 2304.</p><p>2c) Year 2 - Record an allowance to reflect impairment of the loan (assume 50%)</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Bad debt expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51732</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F122/F119</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3462</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Allowance for doubtful loans</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13379</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F412/F119</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>7021</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> The fact that the borrower has already defaulted on the loan once raises questions 
regarding the ability of the department to collect on the loan. Hence an allowance for doubtful loans is recorded. The department 
is able to record an allowance as the disbursement, which established the loan receivable, was charged to a budgetary appropriation.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> There is no impact on appropriations. "F122-Allowances set up for bad debt 
expenses" and "F412-Changes to allowances for doubtful accounts" are used. Alternatively, "F119-Expenditures previously 
charged to appropriations - other amounts to be charged to program expenses" could be used on both sides of the entry.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> There is no impact on economic objects. Bad debt expense is a non-cash expense, therefore 
it falls under standard object 12 and sub-category 34, "3462 -Allowance for bad debts". For a non-cash item related to assets 
and liabilities, sub category 70 is used, "7021 - Allowance for valuation of financial claims".</p><p>3) Year 3 - The department determines that the loan should be written-off</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Bad debt expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51732</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F122/F119</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3462</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Allowance for doubtful loans</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13379</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F412/F119</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>7021</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Loans/advances on expired loan guarantees</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13371</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5399</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> The allowance for $50,000 established in entry 2c is reversed and an additional 
expense of $50,000 is recorded for the remaining balance of the loan.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> There is no impact on appropriations. "F122-Allowances set up for bad debt 
expense" and "F412-Changes to allowances for doubtful accounts" would be used. Alternatively, "F119-Expenditures previously 
charged to appropriations - other amounts to be charged to program expenses" could be for these two lines. R300 is used 
for the other side of the transaction.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> Since there is a change in receivables "5399-Net change to accounts receivable" would 
be used. 7021 is used for the allowance for doubtful accounts while 3462 is used for the bad debt expense.</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement and Presentation Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>Because loan guarantees are contingent liabilities, departments will include only high-level note disclosure. See TBAS 
3.6 Contingencies.</p></section><section anchor="4.4" title="4.4 Future Site Restoration Costs"><h4>Introduction</h4><p>Future site restoration costs encompass costs for dismantling, abandoning and cleaning up a property. These costs may 
be incurred as a result of a contract or because the government has established a policy to restore a site. When such costs 
can be reasonably estimated, they should be accrued (net of expected recoveries), as part of the capital asset and amortized 
over its useful life. The provision for future site restoration costs is to be recorded as a liability until the future 
site restoration takes place. Where future site restoration costs are expected to be significant but cannot be reasonably 
estimated, a contingent liability should be reported.</p><p>Costs to capitalized exclude costs related to environmental liabilities due to contaminated sites and solid waste landfills. 
Accounting and disclosure requirements for these costs will be communicated once the Policy on Accounting for Costs and 
Liabilities Related to Contaminated Sites is finalized.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li>TBAS 3.1 Capital Assets</li><li>CICA 3060.39</li></ul><h4>Scenario A</h4><p>A department constructs an observation tower on leased land, with the condition that it restores the site to its original 
condition at the end of the lease term. The tower cost $100,000 to construct and it is estimated to cost $10,000 to dismantle 
and remove the tower at the end of the ten-year term.</p><p>1) To record cost of tower and future site restoration costs</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Works and infrastructure</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16113</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B14A(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1339</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Works and infrastructure</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>10,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16113</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F129</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>7099</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR GST refundable advance account</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>7,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13392</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>G111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8171</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Future site restoration costs</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>10,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>24112</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>107,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> The $10,000 in future site restoration costs is capitalized as part of the asset 
balance. The $10,000 credit is to a liability account that will remain until the restoration work is performed in ten years 
time.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> (*) In this example it is assumed the cost of the observation tower would 
be charged to the capital vote. However, depending on the department and the asset involved, the following authority codes 
could be used: B11A- Program vote, B12A -Operating vote, or A131 Spending of amounts equivalent to proceeds from disposal 
of surplus Crown assets. As the costs associated with the future site restoration will only be incurred in the future, "F129 
-Other amounts to be charged later" is used. Since GST is not to be charged to a departmental appropriation, it is set up 
as an advance under a special authority, G111. There is no impact on authorities for the accounts payable and future site 
restoration costs liability hence R300 - All other assets and liabilities" is used.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> "1339- Other engineering works" is used to record the observation tower. The recording 
of the future site restoration costs would have no impact economic objects as these are recorded on an expenditure basis; 
"7099- Net increase or decrease in other transactions" is used. Since there is GST/HST payable, the GST is reflected by 
using "8171 - Payment of GST on purchases". "6299 - Net increase or decrease to other liability accounts" is used for the 
two liability accounts.</p><p>2) Record amortization of the observation tower</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Amortization expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51413</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3451</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accumulated amortization</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16213</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F311</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>7061/7099</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> Using straight-line amortization of 10 years, the cost of the asset and the future 
site restoration is allocated over the life of the asset (110,000/10 years).</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> Expenditures for the acquisition were charged to an appropriation in the 
previous journal entry, therefore the appropriations are not affected in this journal entry. To assist with departmental 
reconciliation, F codes are used for these non-appropriated amounts. "F111- Expenditures previously charged to appropriations/Amortization 
expenses for capital assets" is used for amortization expense and "F311-Non-appropriated amounts added to or deducted from 
asset balances/ Increases (decreases) to accumulated amortization of capital assets" is used for accumulated amortization.</p><p><strong>Object Coding Rationale:</strong> As these are non-cash (non-expenditure) items, they have no effect on economic 
objects." 7061-Accumulated amortization on capital assets" is used to capture accumulated amortization. Alternatively, "7099-Net 
increase or decrease in other transactions" may also be used. "3451-Amortization expense for capital assets" is used to 
capture amortization expense.</p><p>3) Record the actual restoration costs: Ten years have passed, the demolition of the tower and clean-up costs amount 
to $12,000.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Future site restoration costs</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>10,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>24112</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0819</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Other miscellaneous expenses</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>2,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51729</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0819</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>12,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> The liability of $10,000 that was recorded in entry 1 to record the future site 
restoration costs is credited. The additional costs of $2,000 would be recorded as an expense of the current year.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> The restoration costs would be charged to the operating or program vote, 
as appropriate. Accounts payable has no impact on authorities hence <strong>"</strong>R300 - All other assets and liabilities" 
is used</p><p><strong>Object Coding Rationale:</strong> The economic object used for the restoration costs is "0819 - Non-professional 
personal service contracts not elsewhere specified". "6299 - Net increase or decrease to other liability accounts" is used 
for accounts payable.</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement and Presentation Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>Where future site restoration costs are expected to be significant but cannot be reasonably estimated, a contingent liability 
should be reported. See section 9.4 Contingencies and TBAS 3.6 Contingencies for guidance.</p></section></chapter><chapter anchor="5.0" title="5.0 Net Assets (Liabilities)"><h4>Introduction</h4><p>Net Assets/Liabilities represent the difference between total assets and liabilities. When the total assets exceed total 
liabilities, the resulting amount represents Net Assets. When total liabilities exceed total assets, the resulting amount 
represents Net Liabilities.</p><p>The Net Assets/Liabilities portion of the Statement of Financial Position can be broken down into two categories i.e. 
unrestricted Net Assets/Liabilities and restricted Net Assets/Liabilities.</p><h4>Unrestricted Net Assets/Liabilities</h4><p>As a minimum, all departments will have an unrestricted Net Assets/Liabilities component made up of the departmental 
Financial Reporting Account 32DDD, where DDD represents the departmental number.</p><p>Transactions that flow through this unrestricted account of the Net Assets/Liabilities at year end are the:</p><ul><li>closing entries associated with revenues accounts;</li><li>closing entries associated with expense accounts and;</li><li>Cash Reconciliation Control Accounts (6XDDD).</li></ul><h4>Restricted Net Assets/Liabilities</h4><p>Some departments may also have a restricted portion of their Net Assets/Liabilities. This portion of the Net Assets/Liabilities 
would be an earmarking of accounts which the government wishes to restrict for specific purposes. These accounts are contained 
in Financial Reporting Accounts in the 312XX range and consist primarily of consolidated specified purpose accounts.</p><p>Consolidated specified purpose accounts are special categories of revenues and expenditures which report transactions 
of certain accounts where enabling legislation requires that revenues be earmarked, and that related payments and expenses 
be charged against such revenues. They are used principally where the activities are similar in nature to departmental activities 
and the transactions do not represent liabilities to third parties but in essence constitute Government revenues and expenditures.</p><p>Further, enabling legislation requires that the transactions in each of these accounts be accounted for separately. (Volume 
1, Section 4.10 of the 1999-2000 Public Accounts).</p><p>For all intents and purposes, these accounts are Internally Restricted Entities as defined by PS 3100.20. Please see 
the special purpose account section of the manual for additional information.</p><h4>Accounting for Restricted Net Assets</h4><p>These accounts are identified in the Equity portion of the COA as FRA 312XX.The transactions of these accounts are recorded 
in revenues (FRA 426XX) and expenses (FRA 516XX) as applicable, in order to provide a more comprehensive reporting of the 
Government's operating results. As a result, these revenue and expense accounts must be closed separately into the relevant 
(312XX) account. They are not closed to Unrestricted Net Assets/Liabilities as are all other revenue and expense accounts.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li>PS 3100</li><li>TBAS 1.2 Departmental and Agency Financial Statements</li><li>Volume 1, Section 4.10 of the 1999-2000 Public Accounts</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Closing of Items to Unrestricted Net Assets/Liabilities</h4><p>The following is a partial listing of accounts that will be used to highlight the closing of items to Restricted and

Machinery and Equipment</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>52,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51421</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0000</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Cash Deposit Control Account</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>300,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>62DDD*</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight">
</td></tr></table><p>* DDD refers to department number.</p><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> Revenues and expenses are temporary (nominal) accounts only intended to be used 
for one fiscal period. They are intended to report a department's financial performance, which is always reported on a period-by-period 
basis. In the long term, net losses or gains are reflected in 32DDD, "Net Equity Advanced". Therefore, at the end of each 
period, the revenue and expense accounts must be "closed" to this Equity account. This is done by reducing the balance in 
the revenue and expense accounts to zero, and adding their balances to Equity. If an account carries a debit balance (like 
an Expense), it must be credited in the amount of its balance, and Equity must be debited for the same amount. So in this 
entry, all revenue accounts have been debited, because they carry credit balances, and all expense accounts have been credited 
because they carry debit balances. The difference between Revenues and Expenses is entered into the Equity account. In this 
case, there are more Expenses than Revenues, so a debit is entered.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> This is strictly an accrual transaction, so the Authority codes are not 
involved. Therefore, all amounts are coded 0000.</p><p><strong>Object Coding Rationale:</strong> This is strictly an accrual transaction, with no impact on the Objects. Therefore, 
all amounts are coded 0000.</p><p><strong>Scenario B - Closing of Items to Restricted Net Assets/Liabilities</strong></p><p>Restricted Net Assets and Liabilities are disclosed separately, therefore they are not closed into the same Equity account 
as unrestricted assets and liabilities. The accounts they are closed in to are more specific, and require separate entries.</p><p><strong>Journal Entries</strong></p><p>1) Restricted Revenues and Expenses are closed to their appropriate
