Schedule of such as part of their financial statement package. Please see TBAS 1.2 Departmental and Agency Financial Statements.</p></chapter><chapter anchor="6" title="6.0 Revenue"><p>Revenues are increases in economic resources, either by way of inflows or enhancements of assets or reductions of liabilities, 
resulting from the ordinary activities of a department. They can result from activities such as the sale of goods, gain 
on sales of assets, interest and penalties earned on tax and non-tax revenue, and return on investments. The manual will 
only explore non-tax revenue.</p><p>Revenues appear on the departmental Statement of Operations, where they are netted against expenses to determine the 
net cost of each business line in the department. Revenues by type are disclosed by way of a Schedule to the Financial Statements.</p><section anchor="6.1" title="6.1 Respendable versus Non-Respendable Revenue"><h4>Introduction</h4><p><strong>This section addresses non-tax revenues only.</strong> (Tax revenues are not addressed in this manual, as they 
only apply to CCRA.). Non-tax revenue transactions can be external or internal to the Government and can be <em>respendable</em> 
or <em>non-respendable</em>. Departments require specific authority to be able to respend revenues, either through a voted 
appropriation or in a statutory appropriation, or specific legislation.</p><p><em>Revenue</em> is defined as the inflow of cash, receivables or other consideration arising in the course of the ordinary 
activities of the government entity, normally from the sale of goods, the rendering of services, and the earning of interest, 
royalties and dividends. It does not include borrowings, such as debenture proceeds, or transfers from other funds or include 
repayments of loans, receivables, advances, etc.</p><p><em>Deferred Revenue</em> is defined as the inflow of cash, receivables or other consideration arising in the course 
of the ordinary activities of the government entity BEFORE the transactions or events occur that give rise to the earning 
of the revenues. (See section on Deferred Revenues) Only after the government meets the obligation for which it collected 
those funds can the transactions be recognized as actual revenue.</p><p><strong>Revenue Recognition</strong></p><p>Revenues should be accounted for in the period in which the transactions or events giving rise to the revenues occurred. 
For example, user fees are recorded in the period when the goods or services are provided, sales when the sales are made 
and revenue from cost sharing arrangements when the costs are incurred to earn that revenue. Revenues should be recognized 
based on the revenue recognition criteria set out in the CICA handbook [Section 3400.6 to 3400.15] and for administrative 
simplicity, they are normally recorded at the time the invoice is issued. However, care must be exercised when goods or 
services are provided near the end of a particular accounting period since revenues must be recognized in the period even 
though an invoice may not have been issued. This can be accomplished through setting up an accrued or accounts receivable. 
Items not practically measurable until cash is received would be accounted for at that time. (PS 1500.83)</p><p><strong>Examples of Non-Tax Revenues include:</strong></p><ul><li>Sales of goods and services to parties outside or within the government</li><li>Gain on sales of assets (both capital and non-capital)</li><li>Interest and penalties earned on tax and non-tax revenue</li><li>Revenue on consolidated and non-consolidated Specified Purpose Accounts</li><li>Revenue from Cost Sharing Arrangements (other)</li><li>Return on Investments</li><li>Consolidated Crown Corporation revenue</li><li>Other non-tax revenue</li></ul><h4>References</h4><ul><li>PSA 1500.83-1500.87, 1800.37-1800.40</li><li>CICA Handbook Sections 1000.37, 3400</li></ul><h4>Scenario A1 - External Transactions - Non respendable</h4><p>The department sells information products to an outside party for $500. (Assumption: Sale takes place in Ontario. See 
section on Sales Tax for rules on sale tax with respect to sales in other provinces.)</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) Department has delivered information products to an outside party for $500</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Accounts receivable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>575</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11221</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5399</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR GST payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>35</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21134</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR PST payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>40</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21151</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Sales of goods and information products</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>42315</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>D/E(*)</p></td><th scope="row" class="alignTopRight"><p>4546</p></th></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>Note: The entries for the settlement of GST payable can be found in the section related to Sales Tax Section. Entries 
required when the accounts receivable is paid are covered in the Accounts Receivable section of this manual.</p></div><p><strong>FRA Coding rationale:</strong> At this point the Department should recognize the revenue since the amount is 
known and the risks and rewards of ownership have been transferred to the buyer and the seller has completed all significant 
acts. Once the goods have been provided, the revenue should be recorded in the Department's books, as well as the relevant 
GST and PST that is payable on the revenue. Assuming this transaction takes place in Ontario, the PST payable is calculated 
as 8% of the sale price and is a payable to the Ontario Government in accordance with the applicable provincial government 
requirements for reporting and remitting provincial sales taxes. The GST payable is calculated as 7% of the sales price 
and is payable to Canada Customs and Revenue Agency. A receivable must be set up to record the amount to be received (which 
includes the GST and PST) by the outside party. Where an invoice has not been issued, an accrued receivable for an estimated 
amount should be set up using FRA 11223 and ignoring the GST and PST payable. This accrual can be reversed in the next period 
before the invoice is issued.</p><p><strong>Authority code rationale:</strong> Since there are no impacts on the authorities for payables and receivables 
"R300- All other assets and liabilities" is used. D/E(*) With respect to revenue, depending on the nature of the revenue 
any of the following applicable codes could be used: </p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopCenter"><p><strong>Statutory Non-Tax Revenue</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopCenter"><p><strong>Non Statutory Non-Tax Revenue</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p><strong>Non-Respendable Revenue</strong></p></th><td class="alignTopCenter"><p>D221 to D223</p></td><td class="alignTopCenter"><p>E221 to E223</p></td></tr></table><p>Please note that these D and E codes capture the relevant revenue charging authority. D is used for those which are statutory 
whereas E captures those which are non-statutory. These do not affect appropriations, and no further entries for authorities 
are required when the cash is received from the customer.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> "To record the GST Payable and PST payable "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to 
Other Liability Accounts" would be used. "5399 - Net Change to Accounts Receivable" is used to establish an accounts receivable. 
At this point the revenue is earned, therefore the object is affected. "4546-Sales of information products" would be used 
in this particular Scenario. However, depending on the nature of the good or service provided, the appropriate non-tax 
revenue object (45xx or 48xx) would be used.</p><h4>Scenario A 2 - Internal Transactions - Non-respendable</h4><p>There is no conceptual difference between transactions with external parties and those with other government departments 
but there are procedural differences. The major difference is that, for sales of goods and services, the billing department 
(creditor) does not have to wait for payment by the invoiced department (debtor). Instead, the creditor is deemed to have 
been paid when a transaction is processed by the Interdepartmental Settlement functionality of the Standard Payment System 
(SPS/IS). The Receiver General Manual should be consulted for more information on the Interdepartmental Settlement process.</p><p>For the purposes of the accounting transactions, there is no requirement for the creditor department (the selling department) 
to affect accounts receivable with the new FIS Interdepartmental Settlement (IS) process, and to separate the billing process 
from the settlement process for their revenue transactions. However, for the following reasons it may be advantageous to 
use the Accounts Receivable functionality of your financial system, especially if there are multiple potential sources of 
IS initiation, for example, more than one billing or invoicing system:</p><ul><li>Single point for the processing of transactions to and from SPS/IS,</li><li>Centralized record of transactions per customer,</li><li>More accurately reflects cross-year transactions (revenue earned in one fiscal year, IS initiation in the following 
  fiscal year)</li></ul><p>May facilitate reconciliation with the IS Control Accounts.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) Department has sold goods to another department for $500</p><div known and the risks and rewards of ownership have transferred to the buyer as well the seller has completed all significant 
acts. The Department is deemed to have been paid on successful processing of the transaction through SPS/IS; the IS Debit 
Control Account is used on receipt of the return file from SPS/IS. (Departments are not obliged to use the "In Transit" 
accounts. The alternative is to affect the Control Account on initiation of the transaction to the Receiver General system 
and adjusting for any rejected items after receipt of the appropriate return file.)</p><p><strong>Authority code rationale:</strong> D/E(*) See Scenario A1, Journal Entry 1, Authority Code Rationale. Since there 
is no impact on authorities with respect to Transit accounts R300 is used, All RG Interface Control Accounts are zero-filled.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> "5399-Net Change to Accounts Receivable" is used to establish an interdepartmental 
account receivable. To record the net impact on Cash Accounts, 5299 would be used. "4546-Sales of information products" 
should be used in this particular Scenario. But depending on the nature of the good or service sold the appropriate non-tax 
revenue object in sub-categories 45, 46, or 48 would be used. 9DDD is used for interdepartmental settlements.</p><h4>Scenario B1 - External Transactions - Respendable</h4><p>The department sells information products to an outside party for $500. (Assumption: Sale takes place in Ontario. See 
section on Sales Tax for rules on sales tax with respect to sales in other provinces.)</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) Department has delivered information products to an outside party for $500</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Accounts receivable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>575</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11221</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5399</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>PST payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>40</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21151</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>GST payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>35</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21134</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Sales of goods and information products</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>42315</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>D/E(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4546</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>Note: The entries for the settlement for GST payable can be found in the section related to Sales Tax. Entries required 
when the accounts receivable is paid by customers are covered in the Accounts Receivable section of this manual.</p></div><p><strong>FRA Coding rationale:</strong> At this point the Department should recognize the revenue since the amount is 
known and the risks and rewards of ownership have transferred to the buyer as well the seller has completed all significant 
acts. Once the goods have been provided, the revenue should be recorded in the Department's books, as well as the relevant 
GST and PST that is payable on the revenue. Assuming this transaction takes place in Ontario, the PST payable is calculated 
as 8% of the sale price and is a payable to the Ontario Government in accordance with the applicable provincial government 
requirements for reporting and remitting provincial sales taxes. The GST payable is calculated as 7% of the sales price 
and is payable to Canada Customs and Revenue Agency. A receivable must be set up to record the amount to be received (which 
includes the GST and PST) by the outside party. Where an invoice has not been issued, an accrued receivable for an estimated 
amount should be set up using FRA 11223, but ignoring the GST and PST payable.</p><p><strong>Authority code rationale:</strong> Since there are no impacts on the authorities for payables and receivables 
"R300- All other assets and liabilities" is used. D/E(*) With respect to revenue, depending on the nature of the revenue 
any of the following applicable codes could be used:</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopCenter"><p><strong>Statutory Non-Tax Revenue</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopCenter"><p><strong>Non Statutory Non-Tax Revenue</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTopCenter"><p><strong>Respendable Revenue</strong></p></th><td class="alignTopCenter"><p>D211 to D213</p></td><td class="alignTopCenter"><p>E211 to E213</p></td></tr></table><p>Please note that these D and E codes capture the relevant revenue charging authority. D is used for those which are statutory 
whereas E captures those which are non-statutory. These do not affect appropriations at this stage, but further entries 
for authorities are required when the settlement is received from the customer.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> To establish the PST and GST payable "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other 
Liability Accounts" would be used. "5399 - Net Change to Accounts Receivable" is used to establish an accounts receivable. 
At this point the revenue is earned, therefore the object is affected. "4546-Sales of information products" would be used 
in this particular Scenario , as this amount is respendable revenue that is included in standard object 13. However, on 
the nature of the good or service provided, the appropriate non-tax revenue object in sub-category 35 would be used.</p><p>2) Subsequently, the invoice is paid in full and revenue is credited to the vote (Department has authority to respend)</p><div class="indent1"><p>2a) Outside party pays invoice in full</p></div><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Cash in Hands of Depts<br></br>
    (awaiting deposit to RG)</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>575</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11125</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts receivable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>575</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11221</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5399</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p><strong>See Cash section for further entries related to the settlement of Cash in Hands of Departments (awaiting deposit 
  to RG).</strong></p></div><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> At this point the outside party has paid the department thereby reversing the 
accounts receivable and increasing the Department's "Cash in hands of Depts (awaiting deposit to RG)" holdings.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> Since there is no effect on appropriations with respect to the settlement 
of the accounts receivable, R300 is used.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> To record the net impact on Cash Accounts, 5299 would be used. To indicate 
the net impact on accounts receivable" 5399-Net Change to Accounts Receivable" is used.</p><div class="indent1"><p>2b) Now that the revenue has been received, it can be credited to departmental appropriations (i.e. as respendable 
  revenue)</p></div><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Sales of goods and information products</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>42315</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>D218/E218</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>7099</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Sales of goods and information products</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>42315</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B13A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>7099</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA rationale:</strong> This transaction is strictly recorded for authority purposes only. To ensure there is 
no effect on FRAs, the same FRA is debited and credited for the same amount.</p><p><strong>Authority rationale:</strong> When a Department has authority to re-spend revenue, it can only be respent when 
the revenue is actually received (i.e. on a cash basis). Only the revenue portion of the transaction is affected-in this 
case, $500. To reflect this, the cash received is credited to "B13A Revenues credited to the vote". The debit will be to 
either a D218 (statutory) or E218 (non-statutory) depending on where the original sale was recorded. It is important that 
either D218 and E218 be used in this transaction and that the authority code used to set up the revenue transaction not 
be used. Otherwise, information on the revenue charging authorities would be lost.</p><p><strong>Object rationale:</strong> This is strictly an authority transaction. To ensure there is no effect on objects, 
the same object, "7099- Net Increase or Decrease in Other Transactions", is debited and credited for the same amount so 
it will have a nil effect on objects.</p><h4>Scenario B2 - Internal Transactions - Respendable</h4><p>As with transactions with external parties, the only differences between the entries for respendable revenue and those 
for non-respendable revenue are the authority code used on the recognition of Revenue and the requirement to affect the 
authority for Revenue Credited to the Vote.</p><p>The authority code rationale in Journal Entry 1 in Scenario B1 applies to the entry to recognize revenue used in the 
first journal entry of Scenario A2, regardless of whether Accounts Receivable is used or not.</p><p>The same transaction as Journal Entry 2b of Scenario B1 must be recorded whenever the Department considers itself to 
have been "paid".</p><h4>Scenario C - Recognition of Gains on Sales of Assets</h4><p>See Tangible Capital Asset Section</p><h4>Scenario D - Interest Revenue on Overdue Receivables</h4><p>An outside party is overdue in paying their trade receivables for goods sold to them by the Department. The Department 
is owed $50 in interest on these overdue accounts receivable.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) Record interest on non-tax revenue</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Accounts receivable non-tax revenue</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11221</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5399</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Interest on overdue accounts receivable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>42541</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>E500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4832</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Since the amount of revenue is measurable and ultimate collection is reasonably 
assured, the department will recognize $50 in interest revenue on overdue accounts receivable. Since the amount is yet to 
be received from the outside party, an accounts receivable is set up. If the department wants to separate these receivables 
from the regular receivables, FRA 11223 is available for this purpose.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> There is no impact on authorities with respect to receivables, R300 is used. 
"E500 - All other non-tax revenue" would be used in this Scenario since there is no other specific authority to capture 
this information. It should be noted that this authority is credited on an accrual basis and not when the cash is received.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> 5399 is used to establish an accounts receivable. "4832-Interest on overdue 
accounts receivable" is used to indicate that the revenue has been earned. If the original revenue is respendable, object 
3593 should be used instead of 4832.</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement Presentation and Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>Revenues are to be recorded by program and business line on the Department's Statement of Operations. The amounts of 
individual items that make up the total non-tax revenue of the Department are to be captured in the Schedule of Non-tax 
Revenues.</p></section><section anchor="6.2" title="6.2 Unrestricted Gifts, Bequests, Donations"><h4>Introduction</h4><p>This section applies to the receipt of physical assets through gifts, bequests and donations. This section also applies 
to the receipt of financial assets through gifts, bequests and donations that do not have a specified purpose. Gifts, bequests 
and donations of financial assets that are received for a specified purpose should be accounted for as a specified purpose 
account (see section 9.3).</p><p><strong>Authorities Perspective:</strong></p><p>Any amount received as a gift to the Crown without any condition or requirement as to the use of the amount shall be 
credited to the Debt Servicing Reduction Account.</p><p><strong>Accrual Accounting Perspective:</strong></p><p>Donations are treated differently depending on whether they are restricted donations or unrestricted donations.</p><p><strong>Restricted Contributions:</strong></p><p>If the external parties specify how the resources are to be used, those inflows are restricted in nature. For example, 
a third party could donate a parcel of land, conditional that a building or other structure be built on it. This would constitute 
an external restriction since the asset is restricted by agreement with the external party. Restricted contributions for 
the purchase of capital assets that will be amortized should be deferred and recognized as revenue on the same basis as 
the amortization expense relate to the acquired capital assets (CICA 4410.33).</p><p>It should be noted that a contribution restricted for the purchase of a capital asset or a contribution of the capital 
asset itself is a type of restricted contribution (CICA 4410.02(b(i))).</p><p><strong>Unrestricted Contributions:</strong></p><p>Unrestricted contributions (i.e. cash) should be recognized as revenue in the current period (CICA 4410.47).</p><p>A donated capital asset would be recorded at its fair value at the date of contribution. Fair value may be estimated 
using market or appraisal values. When an estimate of fair value cannot reasonably be made, the capital asset would be recognized 
at a nominal value (CICA 4430.09).</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li><em>Policy on Specified Purpose Accounts</em> - Appendix A Section 4 (available at:
  <a href="/pol/doc-eng.aspx?id=12249">/pol/doc-eng.aspx?id=12249</a></li><li>CICA 4410, 4430</li><li>Debt Service Reduction Act</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Donation of money - No specified purpose &amp; no conditions attached</h4><p>A third party donates $15,000. There are no conditions attached to this gift.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record the receipt of an unrestricted contribution.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Cash in the hand of the Depts awaiting deposit to RG</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>15,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11125</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Gifts to the Crown</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>15,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>42712</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>D341</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4899</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Since this is an unrestricted donation it should be brought into revenue in the 
current period.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> Since the entire amount of revenue is being recognized at this point an 
authority will be affected. In this case, D341-Gifts to the Crown would be credited. The use of this code would alert PWGSC 
that the amount must be reported as part of the Debt Service Reduction Account in the Public Account. There is no impact 
on the authority side for "cash", therefore, "R300-All other assets and liabilities" is used.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> To record the net impact on Cash Accounts, 5299 would be used. To reflect incoming 
revenue in the period "4899-Other non-tax revenue" would be used.</p><h4>Scenario B1 - Contribution is land - without restriction</h4><p>A third party donates land with a fair market value of $12,000. There is no restriction placed by the donor on the use 
of the land.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record the receipt of the donated land.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Land</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>12,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1301</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Gifts to the Crown</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>12,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>42712</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>E500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4899</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Because the contribution of land is without restriction, the fair value of the 
land should be used. The donation is credited to revenue.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale: </strong>"E500-All other non-tax revenue" is used for the revenue side of the transaction as there is no specific authority associated 
with donations of assets. "R300 - all other assets and all other liabilities" is used to record the land. Alternatively, 
"F999 - Non-appropriated amounts" could be used on both sides of the entry as a donated asset has no effect on authorities.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> 1301 would be used for the land and "4899 - Other miscellaneous non-tax revenue" 
would be used for the revenue side.</p><h4>Scenario B2 - Contribution is land - with restriction</h4><p>A third party donates land with a fair market value of $12,000 provided that it be used to build a monument</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record the receipt of the donated land.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop">
DR Land</th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>12,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1301</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Deferred Revenue</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>12,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21510</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>E500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4899</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> As the donation of land has a restriction which has not yet been fulfilled, the 
donation cannot yet be recognized as revenue.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> "E500-All other non-tax revenue" is used for the deferred revenue side of 
the transaction as there is no specific authority associated with donations of assets. "R300 - all other assets and all 
other liabilities" is used to record the land. Alternatively, "F999 - Non-appropriated amounts" could be used on both sides 
of the entry as a donated asset has no effect on authorities.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> 1301 would be used for the land and "4899 - Other miscellaneous non-tax revenue" 
would be used for the revenue side.</p><p>2) The monument is now built, thus the restriction is no longer in effect and the donation can now be recognized in revenue.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Deferred Revenue</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>12,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21510</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F450</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>7099</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Gifts to the Crown</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>12,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>42712</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F259</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>7099</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Once the land is used for the purpose specified, there is no longer a restriction 
on the contribution. Therefore, it is necessary to reduce deferred revenue (the liability) and record revenue.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong>. There is no impact on authorities/appropriations, F codes will be used 
in order to assist in departmental reconciliations. "F450- Other non-appropriated amounts added to or deducted from liability 
balances" would be used for the deferred revenue amount. "F259- Other revenue not being credited to appropriations or other 
authorities at the same time" should be used for the revenue amount.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> Since the object information was recorded at the time of the donation there 
is no impact on the objects for this entry. "7099 - Net increase or decrease in other transactions" would be used for both 
sides of the entry.</p><h4>Scenario C - Contribution is an asset which is above the departmental capital asset threshold.</h4><p>A third party donates equipment with a fair market value of $20,000 and it is required that the equipment be used for 
a specified purpose. The equipment has an expected useful life of two years with no residual value.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record the receipt of the donated equipment.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Machinery and equipment</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>20,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16121</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1243</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Deferred Revenue</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>20,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21510</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>E500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4899</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Contributions of assets should be recognized as increases in revenue. The fair 
value of the asset of $20,000 is credited to a revenue account. Since the fair value of the asset donated is above the Department's 
capital asset threshold, the charge is made to an asset account.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> "E500-All other non-tax revenue" is used for the deferred revenue side of 
the transaction as there is no specific authority associated with donations of assets. "R300 - all other assets and all 
other liabilities" is used to record the land. Alternatively, "F999 - Non-appropriated amounts" could be used on both sides 
of the entry as a donated asset has no effect on authorities.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> Only one side of the transaction will have an impact on the objects. At this 
point equipment has been donated, therefore 1243 would be used. "4899 - Other miscellaneous non-tax revenue" would be used 
for the revenue side.</p><p>2) To record the amortization expense and the accumulated amortization for one month</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Amortization Expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>833</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51433</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3451</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accumulated Amortization</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>833</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16233</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F311</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>7061</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> It is necessary to allocate the cost of the asset as an expense in a rational 
and systematic manner over those periods expected to benefit from the use of the asset. Using straight-line amortization, 
the monthly charge to amortization expense and accumulated amortization would be $833 ($20,000/2yrs = $10,000/year; $10,000/12mths 
= $833/month).</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> Expenditures for the acquisition were charged to an appropriation in the 
previous journal entry, therefore the appropriations are not affected in this journal entry. To assist with departmental 
reconciliations, F codes are used for these non-appropriated amounts. "F111- Expenditures previously charged to appropriations/Amortization 
expenses for capital assets" is used for amortization expense and "F311-Non-appropriated amounts added to or deducted from 
asset balances/ Increases (decreases) to accumulated amortization of capital assets" is used for accumulated amortization.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> As these are non-cash (non-expenditure) items, they have no effect on economic 
objects." 7061-Accumulated amortization on capital assets" is used to capture accumulated amortization. "3451-Amortization 
expense for capital assets" is used to capture amortization expense.</p><p>3) To recognize revenue earned</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Deferred revenue</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>833</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21510</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F450</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>7099</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Gifts to the Crown</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>833</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>42712</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F259</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>7099</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> As the equipment is used for the purpose specified, there is no longer a restriction 
on the contribution. Therefore, revenue is recognized in the same amounts as the amortization expense. The deferred revenue 
account (the liability) is reduced as revenue is recorded.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong>. There is no impact on authorities/appropriations, F codes will be used 
in order to assist in departmental reconciliations. "F450- Other non-appropriated amounts added to or deducted from liability 
balances" would be used for the deferred revenue amount. "F259- Other revenue not being credited to appropriations or other 
authorities at the same time" should be used for the revenue amount.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> Since the object information was recorded at the time of the donation there 
is no impact on the objects for this entry. "7099 - Net increase or decrease in other transactions" would be used for both 
sides of the entry.</p><h4>Scenario D - Contribution is an asset which is less than the departmental capital asset threshold.</h4><p>A third party donates equipment with a fair market value of $4,000 and it is required that the equipment be used for 
a specified purpose.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record the receipt of the donated equipment.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Operating Expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1243</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Gifts to the Crown</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>42712</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>E500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4899</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Contributions of assets should be recognized as increases in revenue. The fair 
value of the asset of $4,000 is credited to a revenue account. Since the fair value of the asset donated is below the Department's 
capital asset threshold, the charge is made to operating expense.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> "E500-All other non-tax revenue" is used for the revenue side of the transaction 
as there is no specific authority associated with donations of assets. "R300 - all other assets and all other liabilities" 
is used to record the land. Alternatively, "F999 - Non-appropriated amounts" could be used on both sides of the entry as 
a donated asset has no effect on authorities.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> Only one side of the transaction will have an impact on the objects. At this 
point equipment has been donated, therefore 1243 would be used. "4899 - Other miscellaneous non-tax revenue" would be used 
for the revenue side.</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement Presentation and Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>Unrestricted gifts, bequests and donations of financial assets are reported on the department's Statement of Operations 
under the heading Revenues.</p><p>Capital assets received as a result of gifts, bequests and donations should be included in the department's disclosure 
of capital assets. See presentation and disclosure requirements in Section 3.5.1.</p></section></chapter><chapter anchor="7" title="7.0 Expenses"><p>Expenses are the cost of resources consumed in and identifiable with the operations of the accounting period. PS 1500.93 
Examples of expenses include operating expenses, grants and contributions, salaries, etc.</p><p>Expenses by business line appear on the departmental Statement of Operations. Expenses by object are reflected in a Schedule 
to the Financial Statements.</p><section anchor="7.1" title="7.1 Operating Expenses"><h4>Introduction</h4><p>The majority of transactions that a department will record relate to operating expenses. These are expenses that the 
departments incur in the course of delivering program outputs. Operating expenses include such items as personnel costs, 
office supplies, capital assets purchases which are below the department's capitalization threshold, repair and maintenance, 
consulting fees, operating leases, etc.</p><p>In addition to the proper accrual accounting treatment, it is important to ensure that the operating expenses are charged 
to the correct appropriation or authority whether it is the program vote, operating vote, capital vote, a statutory authority, 
or a specified purpose account etc. It should also be noted that some expenses e.g. amortization, bad debts and provision 
for accumulated vacation pay are not charged to an appropriation. As well, it is important to ensure that the appropriate 
economic object is selected to reflect the nature of the transaction.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li>TBAS 1.2 Departmental and Agency Financial Statements</li><li>PS 1500.74-.75, 1500.79-.81, 1500.93-.97</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Department incurs consulting fee expenses</h4><p>The Department incurs $8,000 in consulting fees for a feasibility study.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) Consulting for the feasibility study has been completed.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Operating Expenses</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>(**)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0491</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR GST refundable advance</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>560</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13392</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>G111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8171</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable*</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8,560</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>* See Accounts Payable section for explanation on coding and rationale.</p><p>Note: There are further entries required to discharge the accounts payable. Please refer to the Accounts Payable section.</p></div><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Once the operating expenses have been incurred, (regardless of when it is paid 
for or whether the invoice has been received), the Department must record the expenses in the period by debiting "51321-Operating 
Expenses". The consulting fees are recorded as operating expenses. Either a payable must be set up to record the amount 
owing by the Department or an accrued liability if it is for an estimated amount (in this case GST would not be recorded). 
In this example, it is assumed that the Department has been invoiced and hence is being charged GST on the consulting fees 
and must pay it to the vendor. However, as the Department will eventually recover this amount from Canada Customs and Revenue 
Agency (CCRA) they should record it as an asset in "13392 GST/HST Refundable advance accounts".</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> (**) Once the service has been received, (regardless of when it is paid 
for or whether the invoice has been received), the Department would charge an appropriation (either the Program vote - B11A 
or the Operating Vote- B12A). In the event that the expense relates to a SPA, then the operating expenses would be charged 
to the appropriate non-budgetary authority. If the SPA relates to a non-statutory authority then one of the following authority 
codes would be used; P3xx, P5xx, P7xx or P8xx and if the SPA relates to a statutory authority, then either N3xx or N5xx 
would be used. Since GST is not to be charged to a departmental appropriation, it is set up as an advance under a special 
authority, G111.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> At this point the service has been rendered, therefore an economic object has 
to be charged. In this particular instance the expenses relate to management consulting therefore the code " 0491-Management 
consulting" would be used. However, depending on the good or service acquired, the appropriate economic object in sub-categories 
01 to 13 would be used. To record the net impact on Accounts Payable, "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability 
Accounts" would be used. Since there is GST/HST payable, the GST must be reflected by using, "8171-Payment of GST on purchases".</p><h4>Scenario B - Department incurs repair expenses</h4><p>The Department incurs $6,500 in repairs for a heating system for an office building.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) Repairs for the heating system are completed.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Operating Expenses</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6,500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>(**)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0630</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR GST refundable advance</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>455</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13392</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>G111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8171</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable*</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6,955</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>* See Accounts Payable section for explanations of coding and rationale.</p><p>Note: There are further entries required to discharge the accounts payable. Please refer to the Accounts Payable section.</p></div><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> See journal entry Scenario A 1)</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> See journal entry Scenario A 1)</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> At this point the service has been rendered, therefore an economic object has 
to be charged. In this particular instance the expenses relate to the repairs of an office building, therefore, "0630 - 
Repair of Buildings/Office buildings" would be used. However, depending on the good or service acquired the appropriate 
economic object in sub-categories 01 to 13 would be used. To record the net impact on Accounts Payable, "6299-Net Increase 
or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" would be used.</p><h4>Scenario C - Department purchases equipment for less than the Departmental Capital Asset Threshold (maximum $10,000)</h4><p>The Department purchases and receives computer equipment (monitors) for $4,000.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) Purchase and receipt of computer monitors for a cost less than the department's capital threshold.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Operating Expenses</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>(**)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1227</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR GST refundable advance</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>280</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13392</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>G111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8171</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable*</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4,280</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>* See Accounts Payable section for explanations of coding and rationale. There are further entries required to discharge 
  the accounts payable. Please refer to the Accounts Payable section.</p></div><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Since the purchase of equipment is less than the $10,000 threshold the $4,000 
will be expensed instead of capitalized. See journal entry Scenario A 1)</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> See journal entry Scenario A 1) As well this expenditure could be charged 
to the Capital vote B14A, depending on the department's vote structure.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> At this point the service has been rendered, therefore an economic object has 
to be charged. In this particular instance the expenses relate to the purchase of computer hardware, "1227 - Computer equipment 
-small-desktop/personal/portable/keyboard" would be used. This object will be used, regardless of whether the computer monitors 
are capitalized for FRA purposes and the authority code used for appropriation purposes. However, depending on the good 
or service acquired the appropriate economic object in sub-categories 11 to 13 would be used. To record the net impact on 
Accounts Payable, "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" would be used.</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement Presentation and Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>As per TBAS 1.2 Departmental and Agency Financial Statements, operating expenses will be disclosed in total by business 
line on the Statement of Operations and will be broken out by type on the Schedule of Operating Expenses.</p></section><section anchor="7.2" title="7.2 Grants and Contributions"><p><strong>Authorities Perspective:</strong></p><p>A grant is a transfer payment made to an individual or organization which is not subject to being accounted for or audited 
but for which eligibility and entitlement may be verified or for which the recipient may need to meet pre-conditions (<em>Transfer 
Payment Policy)</em>.</p><p>A contribution is a conditional transfer payment to an individual or organization for a specified purpose pursuant to 
a contribution agreement that is subject to being accounted for and audited (<em>Transfer Payment Policy).</em></p><p>For appropriation purposes, grants and contributions are charged to either a Grants and Contribution vote or a Program 
Expenditures vote depending if a department has a separate vote or not.</p><p><strong>Accrual Accounting Perspective:</strong></p><p>Grants and contributions are transfers of money and/or goods from the government to an individual, an organization or 
another government for which the federal government does not:</p><ol class="lower-alpha"><li>receive any goods or services directly in return;</li><li>expect to be repaid; or</li><li>expect a financial return;</li></ol><p>Grants and contributions shall be accounted for in accordance with PS 3410. They <strong>shall be recognized as an expense</strong> 
in the department's Statement of Operations in the period that the events giving rise to the transfer occurred, as long 
as:</p><ol class="lower-alpha"><li>the transfer is authorized;</li><li>eligibility criteria, if any, have been met by the recipient; and,</li></ol><p>a reasonable estimate of the amount can be made.</p><p><strong>Repayable contributions</strong> are those transfers whereby the recipient is expected to repay the amount or 
the government expects to receive a financial return. The terms may specify a calendar date or dates for repayment, or may 
describe the particular time(s) or circumstances(s) that will determine repayment. (PS 3050.07)</p><p>For the accounting treatment of repayable contributions see the following sections of the manual:</p><ol class="lower-alpha"><li>Unconditional Repayable Contributions - See Loans Receivable Section</li></ol><p><strong>Conditional Repayable Contributions - See Conditional Repayable Contributions Section (9.8.1).</strong></p><h4>References</h4><ul><li><em><a href="/pol/doc-eng.aspx?id=13525">Policy on Transfer Payments</a></em></li><li>TBAS 3.2 Transfers (Grants and Contributions)</li><li>PS 3410</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Disbursement of Grant</h4><p>A scholarship is awarded to an individual for $36,000, where $9,000 is given out at the beginning of each year for four 
years, provided the individual stays in the learning institution. It should be noted that if the individual fails to meet 
the requirements of the grant he/she will be required to repay the amounts transferred.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record disbursement of the first instalment, $9,000, to the individual</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Transfer Payments-Scholarship</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>9,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51119</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B15A(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>2041</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>9,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>(See section on Accounts Payable for the entries required for settlement of accounts payable)</p></div><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> At this point, the eligibility criterion for the first instalment has been met, 
the individual is in school, the amount can be estimated and the transfer is authorized. Because the eligibility requirements 
require the individual to be in school only the first instalment can be recognized. An accounts payable is set up for the 
corresponding amount to be paid to the individual. It would be appropriate to establish a commitment for the remainder.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> In this example the grant is charged to the B15A(*) - Grant and Contribution 
vote but depending on the department B11A - Program Vote could be used as well. Since accounts payable has no impact on 
appropriations, R300 is used.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> In this example, the transfer payment is made to an individual, therefore 2041 is 
used. However depending on whom the recipient of the grant is, the appropriate object would be used. "6299- Net Increase 
or Decrease to Other Liability accounts" should be used to indicate the establishment of the accounts payable.</p><p>2) To record disbursement of the second instalment, $9,000 to the individual</p><p>See Journal entry 1</p><p>3) To record disbursement of the third instalment, $9,000 to the individual</p><p><strong>See Journal entry 1</strong></p><h4>Scenario B - Recipient dropped out of school - Required to repay grant</h4><p>In the middle of year 3 the recipient drops out of school and is required to repay $9,000 (only the third instalment, 
conditions were satisfied for year 1 and 2). It has been determined that is likely that recovery will be realized.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) The individual drops out of school and is required to repay grant.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Accounts Receivable for refunds of program expenses</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>9,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11231</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5399</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Transfer Payments-Scholarship</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>9,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51119</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>E500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4731</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>(See section on Accounts Receivable for the entries required for settlement of accounts receivable.)</p></div><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> Once it is certain that full or partial repayment is required, departments will 
set up a receivable and reduce the transfer expenses of the current period.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> Since accounts receivable has no impact on appropriations, R300 is used. 
E500 is used to record revenue from this source for authority purposes.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale</strong>: To indicate the net impact on accounts receivable"5399-Net Change to Accounts Receivable" 
is used. "4731- Repayment of Recoverable Items/ Contribution recoveries" is used to capture the revenue associated with 
the repayment of this grant.</p><p><em>Please note: The appropriate valuation allowance would be recorded. See Accounts Receivable Section, Scenario B.</em></p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement Presentation and Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>Grants and contributions will be recorded as expenses in the Department's Statement of Operations.</p></section><section anchor="7.3" title="7.3 Compensation"><p>Compensation is a major component of a Department's operating expenses. Some components of compensation are recorded 
by the department and others are recorded centrally by Treasury Board Secretariat.</p><p><strong>Employer Pension Contributions</strong></p><p>TBS will not devolve additional responsibilities to the departments with respect to accounting for pensions. All departments 
will continue to record employer contributions as an expense as per the current practice.</p><p><strong>SPA Pension Accounts</strong></p><p>Those departments, responsible for maintaining a specified purpose account (SPA) for Pensions, will continue to account 
for these pensions as per the relevant legislation. Because of these legislative requirements there will be no change in 
the accounting for these pension accounts. However, departments will have to ensure the timely recording of the employer's 
contribution and of the recovery of administrative costs from the account (when applicable) in the month which these transactions 
relate. These departments will also now record a liability in the form of a SPA pension account on their departmental Statement 
of Financial Position.</p><p>Any issues that these departments may have will be handled off-line with Treasury Board Secretariat.</p><p>TBS will continue to amortise any gains and losses and estimation adjustments related to actuarial surpluses or deficiencies 
for Public Accounts presentation</p><p>Please note: Those departments that compensate any of their employees using their own pay systems (i.e. not through the 
PWGSC Pay System) will be handled off-line with TBS.</p><p><strong>TBS will continue to record:</strong></p><ul><li>Amortization of actuarial gains or losses and estimation adjustments related to pensions (allowance for pension);</li><li>Accrued liabilities (allowances) for severance pay;</li><li>Unsigned collective agreements (as per PAYE policy); and</li><li>Other post-retirement benefits.</li></ul><p><strong>Department will record:</strong></p><p>Departments will record all amounts that are provided by the Compensation System at PWGSC. Where amounts are material 
or as stated in a Treasury Board Policy (for example, Policy on Payables at Year-end), Departments should accrue for all 
compensation elements. (See "List of Pay Entitlement Codes" in Appendix A of Master List of Objects - Chart of Accounts 
for the fiscal year 2001-2002 for a complete list of compensation elements.)</p><p>Entitlements that do not affect a departmental appropriation shall not be recorded as an accrued liability (allowance) 
by a Department except for accumulated vacation leave and compensated absences.</p><p><strong>Salaries</strong></p><p>If material to departmental operations, departments will record at month end amounts incurred and payable, such as salaries 
and wages, overtime, retroactive wage and salary settlements, and other entitlements for items such as compensatory leave, 
extra duty, shift work and lay days for ships crews. Departments will also record year-end accruals for amounts incurred 
by March 31 and to be paid after this date for these items (as per instructions in the PAYE policy and Information Bulletin 
of January 27, 2000 called: "Payables at Year-end (PAYE) for FIS and non-FIS departments".</p><p><strong>Retroactive salary settlements</strong></p><p>Retroactive salaries determined by collective agreements negotiated but not paid will be recorded as liabilities by the 
departments under the following conditions:</p><ul><li>When collective agreements have been <strong>ratified and signed</strong> before March 31, the retroactive amounts 
  incurred under the agreement must be charged to the appropriation.</li><li>If the collective agreements have been <strong>ratified but not signed</strong>, the amounts must be accrued, but 
  only upon direction of the Treasury Board Secretariat.</li></ul><p><strong>Other pay accruals</strong></p><p>Amounts owing but not yet paid for severance and separation payments to individuals who have been struck off strength 
by March 31st must also be accrued.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li><strong><a href="/fin/sigs/Information_Bulletins/aatp_info-eng.asp">FY 2001-02 FIS Transition Period -Transition Protocol and Accounting Requirements</a></strong> document issued 
  on November 15, 2000.</li></ul><ul><li>TBAS 1.2 Departmental and Agency Financial Statements</li><li><a href="/pol/doc-eng.aspx?id=12210">Policy on Payable at Year- End (PAYE)</a></li></ul><ul><li>Information Bulletin of January 27, 2000 on: "<a href="/fin/sigs/Information_Bulletins/info_payfis_non-fis_depts-eng.asp">Payables at Year-end (PAYE) for FIS and non-FIS departments</a>"</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Accrued salaries at year end</h4><p>A Department accrues salaries of $400,000 on March 31, 2003. This amount will get reversed out in the new year. The old 
year salary of $400,000 and new year salary expense of $100,000 is paid in new year.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) Old Year Accrual of $400,000</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Salaries and wages</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>400,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51311</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3469/7099</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accrued Salaries and Wages</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>400,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21112</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>(See section on Accounts Payable for the entries required for settlement of accounts payable)</p></div><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> At the end of the year the Department owes its employees amounts that will not 
actually get paid until the next accounting period. These amounts will include basic pay, as well as other material amounts 
such as overtime or performance pay. The Department must record an operating expense for this amount and set up an accrual 
for a corresponding amount.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> In this example the salaries are charged to the B11A(*) - Program Vote but 
depending on the department B12A - Operating Vote could be used as well. Since accrued salaries and wages have no impact 
on appropriations, R300 is used.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> "6299- Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability accounts" should be used to indicate 
the establishment of the accrued payable. Since this is an accrual transaction and economic objects are recorded on an expenditure 
basis, "7099- Net increase of decrease in other transactions" or "3469-Charges to other liability account" would be used.</p><p>2) To record the payment of the salaries for the new year ($100,000) and reverse and pay the accrued salaries of the 
previous year ($400,000).</p><div class="indent1"><p>2a) Reverse the old year salary accrual</p></div><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Accrued Salaries and Wages</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>400,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21112</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Salaries and wages</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>400,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51311</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3469/ 7099</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>2b) Pay New year Salary for the 1<sup>st</sup> week of April ($100,000) and old year salary.</p></div><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Salaries and wages</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>500,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51311</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0102</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Payroll Control Account</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>500,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>63DDD</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0000</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> Entry 2a) is a reversal of entry 1). This amount of $400,000 must be reversed 
in the new year. The new year expense of $100,000 is the net amount charged to salaries and wages expense. The total of 
$500,000 is charged directly to the Payroll Control Account (2b).</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> In entry 1) the salaries of $400,000 were charged to B11A or B12A of the 
previous year. In entry 2a) the new year appropriation is being credited for the same amount (due to reversal requirements) 
and in entry 2b) $500,000 is charged to the appropriation. The net result is that the appropriation is only charged for 
$100,000, which is the new year salary. Please note that the credit to the appropriation is so that the new year appropriation 
is not over-charged when the payment of salaries is made in the new year. Since accrued salaries and wages (which is a payable) 
have no impact on appropriations, R300 is used. Control accounts are zero filled, since they do not impact on appropriations.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> Since 2a) is a reversal entry, the $400,000 (old year salary) is credited to the same 
code used in entry 1. The expenditure of $500,000 in salaries is charged to object "0102- Civilian regular time, part-time, 
seasonal and casual". "6299- Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability accounts" is used to indicate the reduction of 
the accrued payable. All RG interface Control Accounts are zero filled (0000), with the exception of I/S Control Accounts, 

at the object level.</p><h4>Scenario B - Employee transfers from one department to another department</h4><p>For the time being there are no accounting entries required for employees transferred from department to department. 
Year-end accruals will automatically remove those individuals set up at the end of the previous year and will automatically 
include those individuals on strength at the end of year.</p><h4>Scenario C - Unpaid overtime accruals at year-end</h4><p>A Department accrues unpaid overtime of $100,000 on March 31, 2003. This amount will get reversed out in the new year. 
The old year overtime of $100,000 and new year overtime of $50,000 is paid in new year.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) Old Year Accrual of $100,000</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Salaries and wages</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51311</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3469/7099</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accrued Salaries and Wages</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21112</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>(See section on Accounts Payable for the entries required for settlement of accounts payable)</p></div><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> At the end of the year the Department owes its employees overtime amounts that 
will not actually get paid until the next accounting period. The Department must record an operating expense for this amount 
and set up an accrual for a corresponding amount.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> In this example the salaries are charged to the B11A(*) - Program Vote but 
depending on the department B12A - Operating Vote could be used as well. B14A could be used if the salary costs of a particular 
employee are being capitalized. Since accrued salaries and wages have no impact on appropriations, R300 is used.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> "6299- Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability accounts" should be used to indicate 
the establishment of the accrued payable. Since this is an accrual transaction and economic objects are recorded on expenditure 
basis, "7099-Net increase or decrease in other transactions" or "3469-Charges to other liability account" would be used.</p>
2) To record the payment of the overtime for the new year ($50,000) and reverse and pay the accrued salaries of the previous 
year ($100,000). <div class="indent1"><p>2a) Reverse the old year overtime accrual</p></div><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Salaries and wages</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51311</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3469/7099</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>2b) Pay new year overtime ($50,000) and old year overtime ($100,000).</p></div><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" Account</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>150,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>63XXX</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0000</p></td><td
