entries regarding settlement of accounts payable.</p><p>See Sales Tax section for journal entries regarding the settlement of the GST/HST Refundable advance accounts.</p><p><strong>Note:</strong> whether or not GST is charged to the SPA account will depend upon the terms of the agreement 
  with the outside party. If GST is not to be charged, the SPA account would only be charged $16,000 while the GST refundable 
  advance account would be charged $2,800.</p><p>As with the previous transaction, if the department's system cannot accommodate the proposed entry an alternate two-part 
  entry can be performed.</p></div><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> The asset acquired is machinery and equipment, thus FRA "16121" would be used. 
The cost recorded would only be the government's share (60% of $40,000). The SPA liability would be charged the remaining 
cost of the asset (40% of $40,000) plus GST on this balance. GST on the government's share of the purchase (7% of $24,000) 
would be charged to the refundable advance account. The cost of the capital asset plus 7% GST ($40,000+$2,800) would be 
accrued as an accounts payable in the period since expenses were incurred but not yet paid</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> Authorities are charged when there is an acquisition of goods or services. 
Since a capital asset has been acquired, an appropriation or other source of funding must be charged. Only $24,000 should 
be charged to the Departmental appropriation.</p><p>B14A (**) is used in this example, the departmental portion of the acquisition of the asset may also have been charged 
to either B14A - Capital vote, B11A - Program Vote, or B12A Operating Vote, as applicable. The $16,000 (plus GST) not being 
funded from departmental appropriations is charged to the SPA. In this case, N/P(*), either of the following Statutory votes 
can be used depending on the situation - N3xx or N5xx,or, if a non-statutory vote is required, any one of the following 
can be used depending on the situation: P3xx, P5xx, P7xx or P8xx. Since GST is not to be charged to a departmental appropriation, 
authority G111 is used. Accounts payable does not impact an appropriation, therefore, R300 is used.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> Since a capital asset was acquired at this point the appropriate economic object must 
be used. In this Scenario , machinery and equipment were acquired, in which case a 12xx code would be used. Since GST is 
applicable on the acquisition of an asset, the related GST must be reflected using "8171-Payment of GST on purchases". To 
record the net impact on the SPA, "6086 - Payment made in accordance with authorities" or "6099 - Increases or decreases 
in other SPAs" would be used depending on whether detailed object information was desired. "6299- Net Increase or Decrease 
to Other Liability accounts" should be used to indicate the establishment of the accounts payable.</p><p>4) Periodic amortization expense for the capital asset</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Amortization expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4,800</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51421</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3451</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accumulated amortization-Mach. &amp; Equip.</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4,800</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16221</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F311</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>7061/7099</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> The periodic amortization expense of $4,800 is calculated as follows ($24,000/5years) 
It should be noted that the amortization expense is calculated on the cost incurred by the department for the purchase of 
the asset. See Section on Tangible Capital Assets for additional coding rationale.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> See Section on Tangible Capital Assets for coding rationale.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> See Section on Tangible Capital Assets for coding rationale.</p><p><strong>Note:</strong> At the end of the project, the department is allowed to keep the asset under the terms of the 
agreement. The department may choose to record the external party's share of the fair value of the asset as a donated asset 
(at the end of the agreement term). See section 6.2 for accounting entries related to donated assets.</p><h4>Scenario B</h4><p>A department has planned a research project with an estimated cost of $500,000. It enters into an agreement with an outside 
party which calls for the latter to perform the equivalent of $50,000 of research at its own facilities and expense and 
to contribute $100,000 towards any direct expenses incurred by the department on the research project. The agreement does 
not specify which costs are to be paid out of the funds. The outside party will share in the results of the research.</p><p>In this case, the $100,000 provided by the outside party is towards the department's expenses under the research project. 
Hence it would be preferable for the department to reflect the $100,000 received as deferred revenue and record the expenses 
in their accounts. As the expenses are incurred, revenue would be recorded and the deferred revenue account reduced. The 
accounting for the transactions would be identical to those performed in section 9.1.3 for donations and bequests. The only 
the exception is that the revenue account used would be FRA 42734 Revenue from cost-sharing and joint-project agreements 
instead of 42725 Donations and bequest revenue.</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement Presentation and Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>Amounts recorded under cost-sharing agreements will be recorded under the heading Liabilities in the Department's Statement 
of Financial Position. The agreements will either be reflected as liabilities or deferred revenues depending on the accounting 
treatment selected.</p><p>In the notes to the Departmental financial statements, a description of cost-sharing arrangement is to be disclosed.</p><h4>9.1.5 Trust Accounts</h4><h4>Introduction</h4><p><strong>Authorities Perspective (Policy on Specified Purpose Accounts):</strong></p><p>Trust accounts are established to record the deposit of money in the Consolidated Revenue Fund, or the receipt of securities, 
when these funds must be administered by the Government of Canada according to specific terms and conditions of a trust 
agreement or legislation establishing a fiduciary relationship. The funds remain the property of the beneficiary and consequently 
represent a financial obligation of the Government of Canada.</p><p>Transactions recorded in a trust account are limited as follows:</p><ul><li>The receipts and credits will consist of cash and securities received from outside parties or of benefits (and interest, 
  if applicable) payable to beneficiaries directly by the government;</li><li>Charges and payments are limited to the balance in the account and may only be made to or on behalf of the beneficiary, 
  in accordance with the terms and conditions of the trust agreement. When authorized by the legislation or the trust agreement, 
  administrative fees can be also charged to the account.</li></ul><p><strong>Accrual Accounting Perspective:</strong></p><p>Notwithstanding PSAB 1300.33, Departments will record trusts as a liability. This is in compliance with section 21 of 
the FAA.</p><p>Government financial statements should disclose, in a note or schedule, a description of trusts under administration 
by a government or government organization, and a summary of trust balances.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li><em><a href="/pol/doc-eng.aspx?id=12249">Policy on Specified Purpose Accounts</a></em> - Appendix A 
  Section 2</li><li>FAA Section 21</li><li>PSA 1300.36</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Trust Account is set up and payments are made.</h4><p>Department administers funds on behalf of an incapacitated individual. A trust account is established to hold $100,000. 
Any interest earned is accumulated in the trust account. Monthly payments of $500 are made on behalf of the individual for 
his care.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) A trust account is established to hold $100,000 for J. Doe.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Cash in Hands of Depts awaiting deposits to RG</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11125</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Other Trusts (liability)</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>23223</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>N5/P5*</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6081/6099</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>(See section on Cash for the other cash related ledger entries)</p></div><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> The principal amount of the trust is credited to a liability account. The Department 
indicates an increase in its cash holdings by debiting "Cash in Hands of Depts. awaiting deposit to RG".</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> N5/P5*, the trust funds in this case are credited to the authority specific 
to the trust. Either N5xx - Other trust funds set up under various acts" for trusts that are established by legislation 
(statutory) or P5xx - Other trusts and endowments for trusts that are established by a trust agreement (non-statutory).</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> To record the net impact on Cash Accounts, 5299 would be used. To record the impact 
on the SPA "6081-Deposits received" would be used or "6099 -Net Increases or Decreases in Other SPAs" would be used if there 
is no requirement for detailed object reporting.</p><p>2) Trust fund earns interest at a rate 6% per annum - entry must be done by inter-departmental entries and settled via 
inter-departmental settlement (IS) entries.</p><div class="indent1"><p>3a) Creditor side entry by department.</p></div><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" $6,000 (6% x $100,000) on the trust is a public debt charge 
(interest expense). Earnings on the trust increase the liability account. However, as the authority for the interest on 
public debt is under the Department of Finance, the entries must be recorded as O.G.D. receivables\payables until they are 
settled via the IS process.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> As interest is earned on the trust, it will be charged against "A701-Interest 
on unmatured debt" by the Department of Finance. The earnings of the trust will be credited to the same authority as when 
the trust was established.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> "3114 - Interest on SPAs/Interest on Other Liabilities" is used to reflect interest 
charges on the trust fund. To record the net impact on the SPA "6082 - Interest received" would be used or "6099-Net Increases 
or Decreases in Other SPAs" would be used if there is no requirement for detailed object reporting. "5399 - Net increase 
or decrease in accounts receivable" and "6299 -Net increase or decrease in other liability" would be used for the IS accounts.</p><p>3) Money is spent for specified purposes stated in the trust agreement. $500 is spent to meet the individual's expenses 
for the month.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Other Trusts (liability)</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>23223</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>N5/P5</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6086/6099</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> Any money spent out of the trust is debited from the trust account and the corresponding 
amount is set up as a payable for the amount owing.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> Any money spent out of the trust is charged to the same authority code used 
to set up the trust. Since accounts payable does not impact appropriations, R300 is used.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> To record the net impact on the SPA "6086 - Payments made in accordance with authorities" 
would be used or "6099-Net Increases or Decreases in Other SPAs" would be used if there is no requirement for detailed object 
reporting. "6299- Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability accounts" should be used to indicate the establishment of 
the accounts payable.</p><p><strong>Alternate entry: If a department's system cannot handle the above entry, they can perform the entry in two steps:</strong></p><p>First entry:</p><table class="table entries results in the same entry as 3).</p></div><h4>Departmental Financial Statement Presentation and Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>Amounts recorded in trusts accounts will be recorded under the heading Liabilities in the Department's Statement of Financial 
Position.</p><p>In the notes to the Departmental financial statements, a description of trusts under administration by the departments, 
and a summary of trust balances is to be disclosed in accordance with PSA 1300.36.</p><h4>9.1.6 Deposit Accounts</h4><h4>Introduction</h4><p><strong>Authorities Perspective: Policy on Specified Purpose Accounts</strong></p><p>These accounts are used to record the deposit of money belonging to third parties or the receipt of securities when guarantees 
are required from outside parties to ensure compliance of the depositor in accordance with a contract or an agreement. For 
example, contractor securities to ensure satisfactory performance of work (see Scenario A).</p><p><strong>Accrual Accounting Perspective:</strong></p><p>The concept of a deposit account for a specified purpose is in substance a liability from an accrual accounting perspective. 
That is, money received from a third party, that is due back to the third party pending the compliance of the third, is 
recorded as a liability.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li><em><a href="/pol/doc-eng.aspx?id=12249">Policy on Specified Purpose Accounts</a></em> - Appendix B 
  Section 2.2</li><li>PS1500.39</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Contractor Security Deposit</h4><p>A contractor makes a security deposit for $50,000 which is required to ensure that the work performed is satisfactory.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record the receipt of the security deposit.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Cash in the hand of the Depts awaiting deposit to RG</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11125</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Contractor security deposits - cash</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>23232</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>P371</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6081/6099</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Since cash has been received but the contractor has yet to perform his duties, 
a liability is to be set up under "Deposit and Trust Accounts/Contractor security deposits - cash, cheques". The Department 
indicates an increase in its cash holdings by debiting "Cash in Hands of Depts. awaiting deposit to RG".</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> Contractor security deposits received by PWGSC are credited to P371 - Contractor 
Security Deposits. All other deposit accounts are found in the P3xx authority grouping.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> To record the net impact on Cash Accounts, 5299 would be used. To record the 
net impact on the SPA "6081 - Deposits received" or "6099-Net Increases or Decreases in Other SPAs" would be used depending 
on whether detailed object information was desired.</p><p>2) Contractor satisfies all necessary requirements and deposit is returned</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"><p></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Contractor security deposits - cash</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>23232</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>P371</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6085/6099</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>(See section on Accounts Payable for entries related to the settlement of accounts payable)</p></div><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> Since the contractor has satisfied all the necessary requirements, the liability 
is reduced and a payable is set up for the amount owing.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> P371 is debited directly for the amount to be paid back to the contractor. 
Since accounts payable does not affect appropriations, R300 is used.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> To record the net impact on the SPA "6085- Refunds" or "6099-Net Increases or Decreases 
in Other SPAs" would be used depending on whether detailed object information is desired. "6299- Net Increase or Decrease 
to Other Liability accounts" should be used to indicate the establishment of the accounts payable.</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement Presentation and Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>Amounts recorded in deposit accounts would be reported under the heading Liabilities in the Department's Statement of 
Financial Position.</p><h4>9.1.7 Court Awards</h4><h4>Introduction</h4><p><strong>Authorities Perspective: Policy on Specified Purpose Accounts</strong></p><p>Where an award is made to the Crown and it has been stipulated by the court that the moneys are to be used for specific 
purposes, the funds are credited to a specified purpose account and paid out for the specified purposes.</p><p>These funds are considered to be internally restricted assets and are considered consolidated SPAs for financial reporting 
purposes.</p><p><strong>Accrual Accounting Perspective:</strong></p><p>Since the legislation is to be respected, the amount of the court award is not a true liability but is more an earmarking 
of the Net Assets/Liabilities (restricted equity). There are a series of special revenue and expense accounts that will 
get closed separately at year-end into a relevant equity account. With respect to court awards, the funds will flow through 
a specific revenue account (FRA 42635), payments will flow out of specific expense account (FRA 51635) and will subsequently 
get closed out to the related restricted net asset/liability account (FRA 31235) at year end. (see Net Asset/Liabilities 
section of the manual for examples of how these revenues and expenses are closed into restricted net assets/liabilities).</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li><em><a href="/pol/doc-eng.aspx?id=12249">Policy on Specified Purpose Accounts</a></em> - Appendix A Section 7</li><li>PS 3100 Restricted assets and revenues</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - A company is fined and money goes into SPA</h4><p>The courts have found a company guilty of destroying a fish habitat. They have fined the company $100,000 under a section 
of a statute (act). The section of the act specifies that the money received from these fines should be earmarked to reinstate 
the fish habitat. DFO is responsible for the restoration.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) An SPA for the court award is set up.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Cash in Hands of Depts awaiting deposits to RG</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11125</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Fines and other Levies</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>42635</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>L222</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8220</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>(See section on Cash for the cash related ledger entries)</p></div><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> The department shall credit the court award to a special category of revenue and 
the cash in the hands of the department is increased by an equivalent amount.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> The funds are credited to "L222- Fish Habitat Restoration account". Departments 
will be responsible for identifying the specific authority in their departmental systems. Since there is no impact on the 
authority side for cash, R300 is used.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> In this case, funds are coming into the department because of court awards, therefore, 
"8220-Receipts/ Earmarked Fees and Levies" is used. To record the net impact on Cash Accounts, 5299 would be used.</p><p>2) $50,000 in expenses are incurred for the fish habitat.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Payments from earmarked fines other levies</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51635</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>L222</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8225</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>50,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>See Accounts Payable section for journal entries regarding settlement of accounts payable.</p></div><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> As payments are made for the purpose of the restoration of the habitat the money 
is charged to the special category of expenses related to the earmarked revenues. An account payable is established to record 
the amount owing for the expenses that have been incurred but not yet paid.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> The appropriation the fines were credited to, would be the same appropriation 
that the expenses are charged against, L222. Accounts payable does not impact appropriations, therefore, R300 is used.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> Funds used to satisfy the requirements of restoration should be charged to "8225-Payments/ 
Earmarked Fees and Levies". "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability accounts" should be used to indicate the establishment 
of accounts payable.</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement Presentation and Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>Court awards shall be disclosed on the Department's Statement of Financial Position under the heading Net Assets (Liabilities) 
as a restricted asset. The nature, amounts and terms of the court awards should be disclosed in the notes to the financial 
statements.</p></section><section anchor="9.2" title="9.2 Foreign Currency Transactions"><h4>Introduction</h4><p>The Government of Canada's accounting policies are generally consistent with the recommendations of the CICA HB, where 
applicable. However, there is an exception with respect to the recognition of exchange gains and losses on long-term foreign 
currency denominated monetary items. The CICA recommends the deferral and amortization of such gains and losses while the 
Government accounting policy is to include these in net income for the current period.</p><p><strong>Foreign Currency Transactions</strong></p><p>Once foreign currency purchases, sales, inventories, fixed assets or other non-monetary items obtained through foreign 
currency transactions, have been translated and recorded, any subsequent changes in the exchange rate will not affect those 
recorded amounts. CICA 1650.13</p><p>Each asset, liability, revenue or expense arising from a foreign currency transaction should be translated into Canadian 
dollars by the rate of exchange in effect at the transaction date. For example, the transaction date would be the date a 
department would establish a payable on their books as result of purchases made in foreign currencies.</p><p>Departments will record transactions at the exchange rate in effect on the transaction day. This rate could vary with 
the rate in effect on the date the department requisitions the RG for payment. Therefore, on the date of requisition, the 
departments need to record an exchange gain or loss to reflect the differences in exchange rates.</p><p><strong>Restatement at Year-end</strong></p><p>As at March 31, all <strong>monetary items</strong> denominated in a foreign currency shall be adjusted to reflect the 
exchange rate in effect at the balance sheet date. Monetary items can be defined as money and claims to money.</p><p>For example, when the department purchases or sells goods or services on credit with settlement to be in a foreign currency, 
this will give rise to a payable or receivable in that foreign currency. The receivable or payable should be re-measured 
at the equivalent amount of Canadian dollars that would be collected or paid as at March 31.</p><p>Non-monetary items are not restated at March 31, but are recorded and maintained at historical exchange rates (the exchange 
rate in effect at the transaction date).</p><p><strong>Exchange Gains and Losses</strong></p><p><strong>Exchange gains or losses arising on translation or settlement of a foreign currency denominated monetary item 
should be included in the determination of net income for the current period.</strong></p><h4>References</h4><ul><li>CICA 1650</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Foreign Currency Transactions - Loss</h4><p>Department has purchased goods from a U.S firm for $50,000 USD. The exchange rate in effect when goods are received is 
$1.45. A week later the department requisitions the RG for payment. The rate in effect at requisition date is $1.47.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) Department records purchase of goods at time of receipt</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Operating Expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>72,500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A*</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1xxx</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>72,500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>Note: There are further entries required to discharge the accounts payable. Please refer to the Accounts Payable section.</p></div><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Once the operating expenses have been incurred, the Department must record the 
expenses in Canadian dollars at the exchange rate in effect at the time the goods are received. The amount would be recorded 
at $72,500 CDN ($50,000 USD x1.45). A payable must be set up to record the amount owing for the corresponding amount.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> B11A/B12A* Depending on the department's vote structure the department would 
charge the cost of the expenses to either the Program vote - B11A or the Operating Vote- B12A.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> The objects are affected when the transaction is made. Depending on the nature 
of the good, the appropriate code would be used. "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" is used to 
establish an account payable for the amount owing.</p><p>2) Department requisitions Receiver General (RG) for payment.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>72,500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Loss on foreign exchange</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51711</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A*</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3216</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Payments in Transit</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>73,500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11134</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5299</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Since the payment is being requisitioned, the accounts payable is reversed at 
the original amount for which it was established. The Payment in Transit account would reflect the payment requisitioned 
at the rate in effect at requisition date, $73,500 CDN ($50,000 x 1.47). The difference results in a loss of $1,000 ($73,500-$72,500). 
The control account should not be charged until PWGSC has confirmed that the payment has been made.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> The loss would be charged to the departmental appropriation used to record 
the purchase. There is no impact on appropriations with respect to Accounts Payable and payments in Transit, therefore R300 
is used.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> "3216 - Loss on foreign currency transaction" would be used to track these 
types of losses. "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" are used to indicate a settlement of accounts 
payable. To record the net impact on Cash Accounts, 5299 would be used.</p><p>3) The Receiver General (RG) notifies the department that the payment is made at which time the Department will make 
the following entry:</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Payments in Transit</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>73,500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11134</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Payment Control Account - U.S. dollars</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>73,500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>66DDD</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0000</p></td></tr></table><p>DDD - Department number</p><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Once the payment is made, Payments in Transit is reversed and the Payment Control 
account - U.S dollars is credited to reflect that the RG has made the payment.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> Neither of these accounts impacts appropriations. The authority code is 
0000 for the "Payment Control Account -U.S. dollars" and "R300-All other assets and liabilities" for Payments in Transit.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> To record the net impact on Cash Accounts, 5299 would be used. All RG interface 
Control Accounts are zero filled (0000), with the exception of I/S Control Accounts, at the object level.</p><h4>Scenario B - Foreign Currency Transactions - Gain</h4><p>Assume the same situation exists in Scenario A except that the rate in effect at requisition date is 1.43.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4>

The control account should not be charged until PWGSC has confirmed that the payment has been made.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> The gain would be recorded against the departmental appropriation that was 
used to record the purchase. There is no effect on appropriations with respect to Accounts Payable and payments in Transit, 
therefore R300 is used.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" are used to indicate

of foreign currency assets and liabilities" would be the object used to reflect gains related to foreign exchange transactions.</p><p>3) The Receiver General (RG) notifies the department that the payment is made at which time the Department will make
