The exchange rate used to record the payable on the books 
was $1.45 (the transaction date). The payable was recorded at $72,500($50,000 x 1.45). The amount has not been settled by 
year-end.</p><p>The same department also sold goods to a U.S firm for $100,000 USD. The exchange rate used to record the receivable on 
the books was $1.48 (the transaction date). The receivable was recorded at $148,000 ($100,000 x 1.48). The amount has not 
been settled by year-end.</p><p>As at March 31, the exchange rate in place is $1.50</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) Restatement of monetary liabilities at year-end.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>72,500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Loss on Foreign exchange re-valuations at y/e</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>2,500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51712</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>A126</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>3216</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>75,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>(See section on Accounts Payable for the entries required for settlement of accounts payable)</p></div><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> The payable was originally recorded on the books at $72,500. This amount must 
restated to reflect the exchange rate in effect at the balance sheet date. The $72,500 would be removed from the books by 
crediting this amount. The payable is now recorded at the exchange rate present at a year-end $75,000 (50,000 x1.50). The 
difference in rates results in a loss of 2,500 ($75,000-72,500)</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> Since accounts payable has no impact on appropriations, R300 is used. Losses 
for year-end restatement are charged to a statutory authority. Consequently, "A126-Losses on foreign exchange" would be 
used.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale</strong>: "6299- Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability accounts" should be used to indicate 
the establishment of the accrued payable. "3216 - Loss on foreign currency transaction" would be used to track these types 
of losses.</p><p>2) Restatement of monetary assets at year-end.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Accounts Receivable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>150,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11221</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5399</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Gain on Foreign exchange re-valuations at y/e</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>2,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>42732</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>D343</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4892</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Receivable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>148,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11221</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5399</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>(See section on Accounts Receivable for the entries required for settlement of accounts receivable)</p></div><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> The receivable was originally recorded on the books at $148,000. This amount must 
restated to reflect the exchange rate in effect at the balance sheet date. The $148,000 would be removed from the books 
by crediting this amount. The receivable is now recorded at the exchange rate present at a year-end $150,000 (100,000 x1.50). 
The difference in rates results in a gain of $2,000 ($150,000-$148,000).</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> Since accounts receivable has no impact on appropriations, R300 is used. 
Gains related to foreign exchange transactions would be recorded against a statutory non-tax revenue authority, "D343-Gains 
on foreign exchange at year-end".</p><p><strong>Object Rationale</strong>: "5399-Net Change to Accounts Receivable" should be used to indicate the establishment 
of the accounts receivable". 4892-Gain on re-evaluation of foreign currency assets and liabilities" would be the object 
used to reflect gains related to foreign exchange transactions.</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement and Presentation Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>The departments Statement of Operations would include any transaction gains or losses in the calculation of net operating 
results.</p></section><section anchor="9.3" title="9.3 Sales Tax"><h4>Introduction</h4><p><strong>GST/HST</strong></p><p>All GST and HST revenues are to be recorded in the Accounts of Canada on an accrual basis.</p><p><strong>GST/HST on Sales</strong></p><p>Departments must keep the GST and HST charged to their customers on an accrual basis in liability accounts, until the 
amounts are transferred to Canada Customs &amp; Revenue Agency (CCRA).</p><p>Legislation requires that each department and subdivision thereof, designated as a reporting entity for GST and HST purposes, 
must submit to CCRA monthly returns of GST charged. The GST charged is transferred to CCRA in the same period as the return 
is filed, using an Interdepartmental Settlement.</p><p><strong>GST/HST on Purchases</strong></p><p>Departments shall record all GST and HST payable on purchases from external parties, including purchases made on behalf 
of other departments, to the asset account entitled <strong><em>GST Refundable Advance Account</em> (RAA).</strong></p><p>Departments shall transfer these amounts to CCRA on the last working day of March so that CCRA can prepare the Tax Remission 
Order to authorize them to deduct these amounts from the GST Tax Revenue accounts at year-end.</p><p><strong>Provincial Sales Tax</strong></p><p>Provincial sales taxes are calculated in various ways, depending on the province, where the sale takes place. If the 
sale is made in New Brunswick, Nova Scotia, or Newfoundland, the PST is included with the GST and included in the Harmonized 
Sales Tax (HST). The HST is calculated at 15% of the sales price and this whole amount is payable to CCRA. In PEI and provinces 
west of Quebec (except Alberta where there is no PST), the PST payable is calculated as a percentage of the sales price 
(in Ontario it is 8%). It is payable to the provincial government in accordance with applicable provincial government requirements 
for reporting and remitting provincial sales taxes. In Quebec, the QST is calculated as a percentage on the total of the 
sales price plus the GST. The QST is payable to the Quebec government. It should be noted that the Federal Government charges 
PST but does not pay PST.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li><a href="/pol/doc-eng.aspx?id=12195">Policy on the Application of the Goods and Services Tax and the Harmonized Sales Tax in the Departments and Agencies 
  of the Government of Canada For FIS compliant Departments and Agencies</a></li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Department sells goods</h4><p>1) Department has delivered information products to an outside party for $500</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Accounts receivable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>575</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11221</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5399</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR GST/HST payable to CCRA</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>35</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21134</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR PST payable (excluding HST)</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>40</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21151</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Sales of goods and information products</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>42315</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>D/E(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4546</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>Note: Entries required when the accounts receivable is paid are covered in the Accounts Receivable section of this manual.</p></div><p><strong>FRA Coding rationale:</strong> Once the goods have been provided, the revenue should be recorded in the Department's 
books, as well as the relevant GST and PST that is payable on the revenue. Assuming this transaction takes place in Ontario, 
the PST payable is calculated as 8% of the sale price and is a payable to the Ontario Government in accordance with the 
applicable provincial government requirements for reporting and remitting provincial sales taxes. The GST payable is calculated 
as 7% of the sales price and is payable to Canada Customs and Revenue Agency. A receivable must be set up to record the 
amount to be received (which includes the GST and PST) by the outside party. Where an invoice has not been issued, an accrued 
receivable for an estimated amount should be set up using FRA 11223 and ignoring the GST and PST payable. This accrual can 
be reversed in the next period before the invoice is issued.</p><p><strong>Authority code rationale:</strong> Since there are no impacts on the authorities for payables and receivables 
"R300- All other assets and liabilities" is used.</p><p>D/E(*) With respect to revenue, depending on the nature of the revenue any of the following applicable codes could be 
used: </p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopCenter"><p><strong>Statutory Non-Tax Revenue</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopCenter"><p><strong>Non Statutory Non-Tax Revenue</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p><strong>Non-Respendable Revenue</strong></p></th><td class="alignTopCenter"><p>D221 to D223</p></td><td class="alignTopCenter"><p>E221 to E223</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> To record the object for GST payable and PST payable "6299-Net Increase or 
Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" would be used. "5399 - Net Change to Accounts Receivable" is used to establish an 
accounts receivable. At this point the revenue is earned, therefore the object is affected. "4546-Sales of information products" 
would be used in this particular Scenario. However, depending on the nature of the good or service provided, the appropriate 
non-tax revenue object (45xx or 48xx) would be used.</p><p>2) Invoice paid in full</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Cash in Hands of Depts awaiting deposit to RG</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>575</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11125</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CRAccounts receivable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>575</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11221</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5399</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>(Further entries related to cash can be found in the Cash Section of the manual.)</p></div><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> When departments receive payment for the above sales the full amount of the payment 
including the GST/HST shall increase the Department's "Cash in hands of Depts. (awaiting deposit to RG)" holdings. At this 
point the outside party has paid the department thereby reversing the accounts receivable</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> There is no impact on appropriations with respect to the settlement of the 
accounts receivable, therefore R300 is used.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> To record the net impact on Cash Accounts, 5299 would be used. To indicate 
the net impact on accounts receivable "5399-Net Change to Accounts Receivable" is used.</p><p>3) Monthly - GST/ HST transferred by departments to CCRA</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR GST/HST Payable to CCRA</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>35</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21134</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR IS Credit Control Account</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>35</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>65DDD*</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>9122</p></td></tr></table><p>DDD* - Department Number of department submitting sales tax.</p><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Every month the department will transfer the GST/HST to CCRA, this will result 
in the reversal of the GST/HST payable. The payment to CCRA is made through the departments IS credit control account. In 
the month that the sale is to be reported (previous month's sales) on the return to CCRA, the GST/HST payable will be transferred 
by departments to CCRA by Interdepartmental Settlement in that same month.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> There is no impact on appropriations for the GST/HST Payable to CCRA, therefore, 
R300 is used. All RG Interface Control Accounts are zero-filled.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> For GST/HST payable "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" 
would be used. Since this an IS payment to CCRA (tax revenue only) 9122 is used.</p><p>4) Department requisitions RG for payment of PST Payable.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR PST Payable (excluding HST)</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>40</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21151</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Payments in Transit</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>40</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11134</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>(For further entries required to settle the Payments in Transit see the Accounts Payable section of the manual.)</p></div><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> PST is paid in accordance with the applicable provincial government requirements 
for reporting and remitting provincial sales taxes. Since the payment is being requisitioned, the payable is reversed and 
the Payment in Transit account would reflect these payments requisitioned but not yet paid. The control account should not 
be charged until PWGSC has confirmed that the payment has been made.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> Neither of the accounts impacts appropriations, so both sides of the entry 
must therefore be coded to R300-Total amounts of all other assets and liabilities.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" is used to indicate 
a settlement of the PST payable. To record the net impact on Cash Accounts, 5299 would be used.</p><h4>Scenario B - Department purchases goods</h4><p>1) To record the purchase and receipt of a vehicle.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Vehicle</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>24,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16133</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B14A(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1261</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR GST Refundable Advance Accounts</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,680</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13392</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>G111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8171</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>25,680</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale: </strong>The Department must capitalize this asset as a debit to the capital asset (vehicle), 
since the cost is above the $10,000 threshold. Departments are to record the GST or HST due to the suppliers at the same 
time as the related goods or services are recorded to the departmental accounting system. The GST/HST due will be recorded 
in the Refundable Advance Account. The full amount of the invoice will be recorded as an account payable. To further clarify, 
the Department is being charged GST on the vehicle, and must pay it to the vendor. However, as the Department will eventually 
recover this amount from Canada Customs and Revenue Agency (CCRA) they should record it as an asset in "13392 GST/HST Refundable 
advance accounts". Since the Department has not paid for the vehicle, a liability must be recorded for the amount owing. 
It should be noted that the Federal Government does not pay Provincial Sales Tax (PST) on goods and services that it purchases.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> (*) In this example it is assumed this purchase would be charged to the 
capital vote. However, depending on the department and the asset purchased, the following authority codes could be used: 
B11A - Program Vote, B12A Operating Vote, or A131 Spending of amounts equivalent to proceeds from disposal of surplus Crown 
assets. Since GST is not to be charged to a departmental appropriation, it is set up as an advance under a special authority, 
G111. There is no impact on authorities for the accounts payable so the code to be used would be "R300-All other assets 
and liabilities"</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> Economic object 1261 is used in this example since the purchase was a motor 
vehicle. The appropriate economic object is used depending on the nature of the purchase. Since there is GST/HST payable, 
the GST must be reflected by using, "8171-Payment of GST on purchases". "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability 
Accounts" is used to establish the payable for the amount owing.</p><p>2) Department pays the full amount including GST/HST by requisitioning Receiver General (RG) for payment.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>25,680</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Payments in Transit</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>25,680</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11134</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>(For further entries required to settle the Payments in Transit see the Accounts Payable section of the manual.)</p></div><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> Since the payment is being requisitioned, the payable is reversed and the Payment 
in Transit account would reflect these payments requisitioned but not yet paid. The control account should not be charged 
until PWGSC has confirmed that the payment has been made.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> Neither of the accounts impacts appropriations so both sides of the entry 
must therefore be coded to "R300-Total amounts of all other assets and liabilities".</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" is used to indicate 
a settlement of accounts payable. To record the net impact on Cash Accounts, 5299 would be used.</p><p>3) At March 31 of each year GST/ HST transferred by departments to CCRA</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR IS Debit Control Account</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,680</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>64DDD*</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>9122</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR GST/HST Refundable Advance Account</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1,680</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13392</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>G111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8171</p></td></tr></table><p>DDD* - Department Number of department submitting sales tax.</p><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> The department must remove the balance in the GST/HST Refundable Advance Account. 
This is done through a credit to the GST RAA and a corresponding debit to the IS Debit Control Account. Departments are 
to transfer these amounts to CCRA on the last working day of March so that CCRA can prepare the Tax Remission Order to authorize 
them to deduct these amounts from the GST Tax Revenue accounts at year-end.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> There is no impact on appropriations with respect to the receipt of cash 
and accounts receivable, R300 is used. Now that GST is being transferred to CCRA the appropriation G111 must be credited.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> Since this an IS payment to CCRA (tax revenue only) 9122 is used. , "8171-Payment 
of GST on purchases" is credited since the GST is transferring to CCRA.</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement and Presentation Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>Any GST/HST payable not transferred to CCRA will be recorded as a payable under the liabilities section of the Department's 
Statement of Financial Position. This will also be the case for PST payable not yet paid to the relevant Provincial Government.</p><p>Any amounts outstanding in the GST RAA will be recorded as an advance under the Financial Assets section of the Department's 
Statement of Financial Position.</p></section><section anchor="9.4" title="9.4 Contingencies"><h4>Introduction</h4><p>A contingency is an existing condition or situation involving uncertainty as to possible gain or loss to an organization 
that will ultimately be resolved when one or more future events occur or fail to occur. Resolution of the uncertainty may 
confirm the acquisition of an asset or the reduction of a liability or the loss or impairment of an asset or the incurrence 
of a liability.</p><p>Departments and agencies might have contingent liabilities as a result of activities, such as: guarantees of the indebtedness 
of others; claims and pending or threatened litigation; arrangements with international organizations; and insurance programs.</p><p>The uncertainty relating to the future event, which determines the outcome of a contingency, can be expressed by a range 
of probabilities. The probability of the occurrence or non-occurrence of the event establishes the appropriate accounting 
treatment.</p><ol class="lower-alpha"><li>A contingent liability is accrued and recognized as an actual liability in the financial statements if the occurrence/non-occurrence 
  of the future event(s) is likely and the amount of settlement can be reasonably estimated.</li><li>A contingent liability is disclosed in the notes to the financial statements if the occurrence of the future event(s) 
  is unlikely, not determinable or, if determinable and likely, can not be reasonably estimated.</li></ol><p>Departments and agencies are not to recognize a provision on likely and estimable contingencies. Treasury Board Secretariat 
will record a central provision based on the information reported on plates I-11 and I-12 by departments and agencies. TBS 
will review the possibility of devolving these accruals to departments and agencies in the future. Departments will only 
set up a liability once the criteria of the PAYE policy has been met.</p><p><strong>Contingent Gains:</strong> Contingent gains should not be accrued in financial statements as this accounting 
treatment could result in the recognition of revenue which might never be realized. Nevertheless, disclosure of the existence 
of a contingent gain which is considered likely to be realized provides useful information and would, therefore, be included 
in the financial statements.</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement and Presentation Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>Departments and agencies will disclose information in their financial statements to describe their contingencies at the 
end of the accounting period. Disclosure will also be made that no provision for loss is recognized in their financial statements 
but appears only in the Government of Canada consolidated financial statements.</p><p>Refer to Treasury Board Accounting Standard 3.6 - Contingent Liabilities for guidance on the recommended note disclosure 
for financial statements.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li>CICA 3290</li><li>PS 1500.69 -.72</li><li>TBAS 1.2 Departmental and Agency Financial Statements</li><li>TBAS 3.6 Contingent Liabilities</li></ul></section><section anchor="9.5" title="9.5 Commitments"><h4>Introduction</h4><p>Financial commitments, as defined for financial statement purposes, are obligations to outside organizations or individuals 
that will become liabilities if and when the terms of contracts, agreements or legislation are met. (PS 1500.65)</p><p>A commitment is the stage between the establishment of an agreement between parties (whether that be signing a contract 
or passing legislation) and the fulfilment of the requirements of the agreement by one or more parties, creating an obligation 
to perform on the part of the remaining party or parties.</p><p>The most common example of a commitment is contracting for goods or services. Once the contract between the department 
and the supplier has been signed, there is a commitment on the part of the department to perform its part of the contract, 
which, generally, is pay the supplier. The commitment exists until the supplier has performed their part of the contract, 
(i.e., delivered goods or services of a specified nature and/or quality, etc). Once goods or services are received, a commitment 
ceases to exist and the department has an obligation or liability to pay the supplier.</p><p>There may be a fair amount of financial system activity in accounting for commitments. This activity is primarily for 
budget control and to ensure that overspending does not occur. None of the entries involve financial statement classifications 
(asset, liability, expense, revenue or equity) and so should not be termed journal entries but rather memo entries.</p><p>Although committed amounts do not appear on the face of the financial statements, it is necessary to properly present 
the appropriate information for disclosure in the notes. The sample transactions below expand some of the accounting concepts 
related to this area.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li>PS 1500.65 -68</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Department enters into a commitment to purchase vehicles</h4><p>Management in a department decides on February 28, 2003 that it is necessary to purchase 5 vehicles to carry out program 
delivery requirements. The department enters into a contract with an outside party for the purchase of 5 vehicles on March 
15, 2003. The vehicles are delivered on April 21, 2003.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) February 28, 2003</p><p>No journal entry is required. No note disclosure is required.</p><p>There is no commitment at this point. Management has only decided they need the vehicles but have not entered into an 
agreement.</p><p>2) March 15, 2003</p><p>No journal entry is required. Note disclosure is required.</p><p>The department has entered into an agreement to purchase the vehicles, and has committed funds to acquire these goods. 
Since the vehicles have not been received, no liability exists to pay for these goods. As a result, no journal entry is 
required, but note disclosure regarding the nature and amount of the commitment is required on the year end financial statements.</p><p>3) April 21, 2003 - record the liability (purchase and receipt of vehicles)</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Vehicles</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16233</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B14A*</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1261</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR GST/HST Refundable Advance Account</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>7,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>13392</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>G111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>8171</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>107,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>For entries related to the settlement of the GST Refundable Advance Account please see the Sales Tax section of the manual.</p></div><p><strong>FRA coding rationale: </strong>The department must capitalize these assets as a debit to the capital asset (vehicle), 
since it falls above the $10,000 threshold. At this point the department is being charged GST on the vehicle, and must pay 
it to the vendor. However, as the department will eventually recover this amount from Canada Customs and Revenue Agency 
(CCRA) they should record it as an asset in "13392 GST/HST Refundable advance accounts". Since the department has not paid 
for the vehicle, a liability must be recorded for the amount owing.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> B14A* In this example it is assumed this purchase would be charged to the 
capital vote. However, depending on the department and the asset purchased, the following authority codes could be used: 
B11A - Program Vote, B12A Operating Vote, or A131 Spending of amounts equivalent to proceeds from disposal of surplus Crown 
assets. Since GST is not to be charged to a departmental appropriation, it is set up as an advance under a special authority, 
G111. There is no impact on authorities for Accounts Payable so "R300-All other assets and liabilities" is used.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> Economic object 1261 is used in this example since the purchase was a motor 
vehicle. The appropriate economic object is used depending on the nature of the purchase. Since there is GST/HST payable, 
the GST must be reflected by using, "8171-Payment of GST on purchases". "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability 
Accounts" is used to establish the accrual of the amount owing.</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement Presentation and Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>Financial statements should disclose information to describe a government's material financial commitments at the end 
of the accounting period. (PS 1500.66)</p><p>Financial statements should provide information in notes or schedules to describe a government's financial commitments 
that are material in relation to its financial condition or future operations. Such information is useful for understanding 
and assessing future revenue requirements. (PS 1500.67)</p><p>One type of financial commitment relates to the purchase of goods and services to be provided as set out in existing 
contracts, agreements or legislation. This includes commitments for lease agreements and tangible capital asset acquisitions. 
In some circumstances, tangible capital asset acquisitions involve large undertakings. In those circumstances, the costs 
of existing commitments would be accompanied by the estimated total cost of the project. (PS 1500.68)</p><p>Departments and agencies currently prepare information on contractual commitments for inclusion in the Public Accounts. 
Note disclosure for contractual commitments should be similar to that presented in the Government's financial statements. 
However, for the purpose of a department or agency's financial statements, the reporting threshold for commitments should 
be based on the department or agency's level of materiality.</p></section><section anchor="9.6" title="9.6 Environmental Liabilities"><p>At this time, environmental costs will not be recognised in the departmental books of account.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li>Transitional Protocol and Accounting Requirements</li><li>TBAS 1.2 Departmental and Agency Financial Statements</li><li>Policy On Accounting For Costs And Liabilities Related To Contaminated Sites</li></ul></section><section anchor="9.7" title="9.7 Non-Monetary Exchanges"><p>Non-monetary exchanges are exchanges of non-monetary assets, liabilities or services for other non-monetary assets, liabilities 
or services with little or no monetary consideration involved. In general, if the fair value of the monetary consideration 
is less than 10% of the estimated fair value of the total consideration given up or received, the transaction would be considered 
non-monetary. With respect to accrual accounting there are a few different Scenario s with respect to the exchange of non-monetary 
assets with parties external to the Government of Canada.</p><ol class="lower-roman"><li><strong>Assets or services that are exchanged that are dissimilar in nature:</strong> Accounting for exchange of 
  non-monetary assets/services should be based on the fair value of the asset/service given up. The fair value of the asset/services 
  received should only be used if it is clearly more evident than the fair value of the assets/services given up. Any gains 
  or losses on the exchange should be recognised immediately. If the fair value of either asset/service is not reasonably 
  determinable the book value of the asset/service given up is usually used as the basis for recording the non-monetary 
  exchange.</li><li><strong>Assets or services that are exchanged that are similar in nature (involving no monetary consideration):</strong> 
  Similar non-monetary assets/services are those of the same general type, that perform the same function, or are employed 
  in the same line of business. The asset/service acquired should be recorded at book value of the asset/service given up 
  with no gain or loss recognized.</li><li><strong>Assets or services that are exchanged that are similar in nature (involving partial monetary consideration):</strong> 
  When exchanges described in ii) above involve a partial monetary consideration, the carrying value of the asset or service 
  given up would be adjusted by the amount of monetary consideration. The party paying the monetary consideration would 
  record the non-monetary asset/service received at the carrying value of the asset/service given up plus the monetary consideration 
  paid. The entity receiving the monetary consideration would record the non-monetary asset/service received at the carrying 
  value of the non-monetary asset or service given up less the amount of monetary consideration received, unless the non-monetary 
  consideration exceeds the carrying value. In this case, a gain would be recorded for the amount of such excess (CICA 3830.10).<br></br><br></br>Note: transactions between a Department and an outside party that are above $100,000 are to be treated as though they 
  are monetary, i.e. charged to an appropriation. Those below $100,000 would strictly be an accrual transaction in that 
  they do not affect appropriations (F codes should be used). However, where a non-monetary transaction involves a cash 
  component, the amount paid must be charged to an appropriation.</li></ol><p>Any exchange of assets between a department and another entity that is part of the Government reporting entity must be 
performed at the net book value of the asset. The amounts transferred between departments should be gross, that is the cost 
of the asset and the accumulated depreciation. No gain or loss may be recorded in the exchange.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li>CICA 3830.10</li><li>Comptrollership Manual: <a href="/pol/doc-eng.aspx?id=12173">Policy on Accounting for Non-Monetary Transaction</a>, Chapter 5-13</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Exchange of Dissimilar assets/services (for an amount less than $100,000)</h4><p>Department exchanges research equipment plus cash for a service (consulting services) with an outside party. The research 
equipment has a net book value of $42,000 (cost $64,000 less $22,000 accumulated depreciation). The fair market value of 
the research equipment is $49,000. In addition to the research equipment the Department must pay an additional $17,000 cash 
for the consulting services.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record the exchange of dissimilar assets for services for under $100,000.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Operating Expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>49,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F159</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0491</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Operating Expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>17,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>51321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>0491</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Accumulated Depreciation - equipment</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>22,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16229</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F351</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4843</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Equipment</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>64,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16129</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F351</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4843</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Gain on Disposal of Equipment</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>7,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>42411</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>F351</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4843</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>17,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> The consulting service is recorded at the fair value of the item(s) given up (equipment) 
plus the cash $66,000 ($49,000 + $17,000). The equipment and related accumulated amortization would be removed from the 
books, and the cash that will be paid out will be set up as a payable to reflect the amount owing. Since this is an exchange 
of dissimilar items, a gain or loss must be recognized immediately, which would be the difference between the fair value 
and book value of the equipment $7,000 = ($49,000 - ($64,000-$22,000)).</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> Since the fair value of the transaction is less than $100,000, the appropriations 
are not affected for the non-monetary portion of the transaction. Therefore it is necessary to use codes that will show 
a nil effect on appropriations, i.e. F codes. The monetary portion of the transaction, the $17,000 paid, would be charged 
to an operating authority code, either B11A or B12A. There is no impact on the authority side for the accounts payable but 
the system requires that a code be used, in this case it would be "R300- All other assets and liabilities"</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> With respect to economic objects the exchange reflects the acquisition of the 
service and the disposition of the asset. "0491- Management consulting" is used to reflect the receipt of the services. 
"4843-Sales of surplus Crown assets to outside parties" is used to reflect the net value of the disposal and the proceeds 
received for the asset. "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" is used establish an accounts payable.</p><h4>Scenario B - Exchange of Similar assets - no monetary consideration - (transaction is greater than $100,000)</h4><p>Department arranges to exchange with an outside party research equipment (ABC) with a fair value $160,000 and a book 
value of $135,000 (cost $150,000 less accumulated depreciation $15,000) for the XYZ model - research equipment with a fair 
value of $170,000.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record the exchange of similar assets with no monetary consideration.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Equipment(XYZ)</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>135,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16129</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1249</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Accumulated Depreciation-equipment (ABC)</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>15,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16229</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>D321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4843</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Equipment (ABC)</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>150,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16129</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>D321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4843</p></td></tr></table><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> The equipment (XYZ) would be recorded at net book value of equipment (ABC) $135,000 
($150,000 - $15,000) i.e. the book value of the asset given up. The equipment (ABC) and related accumulated amortization 
(ABC) would be removed from the books.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> Since the fair value of the transaction is greater than $100,000 the equipment 
(XYZ) would be charged to the same appropriation as if the transaction was monetary. (*) In this example it is assumed this 
purchase would be charged to the capital vote B14A. However, depending on the department and the asset purchased, the following 
authority codes could be used: B11A - Program Vote, B12A Operating Vote, and A131 Spending of amounts equivalent to proceeds 
from disposal of surplus Crown assets. "D321- Proceeds from disposal of crown assets" is used for the remaining debits and 
credits to reflect the net proceeds received by the Department.</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> With respect to economic objects the exchange reflects the acquisition of an 
asset and the disposition of the asset. "1249- Other equipment and parts" would be used to reflect the receipt of the equipment 
(XYZ). "4843-Sales of surplus Crown assets to outside parties" is used to reflect the disposal and proceeds received for 
the asset given up -equipment (ABC).</p><h4>Scenario C - Exchange of Similar assets - with partial monetary consideration- (transaction is greater than $100,000)</h4><p>Department arranges to exchange with an outside party research equipment (ABC) with a fair value $160,000 and a book 
value of $135,000 (cost $150,000 less accumulated depreciation $15,000) for the XYZ model - research equipment with a fair 
value of $170,000. Department pays $10,000 in cash in addition to the ABC -research equipment exchanged.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record the exchange of similar assets with partial monetary consideration.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Equipment(XYZ)</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>145,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16129</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>1249</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Accumulated Depreciation</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>15,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16229</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>D321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight">
 </td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>- equipment (ABC)</p></th><td class="alignTopRight">
 </td><td class="alignTopRight">
 </td><td class="alignTopRight">
 </td><td class="alignTopRight">
 </td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Equipment (ABC)</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>150,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>16129</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>D321</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4843</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>10,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>See the Accounts payable section for journal entries used to settle this payable.</p></div><p><strong>FRA coding rationale:</strong> The equipment (XYZ) would be recorded at net book value of equipment (ABC) plus 
the additional cash requirement $145,000 ($150,000 -$15,000+ $10,000). The equipment (ABC) and related accumulated amortization 
(ABC) would be removed from the books, and $10,000 owing would be recorded as a payable.</p><p><strong>Authority coding rationale:</strong> Since the fair value of the transaction is greater than $100,000 the equipment 
(XYZ) would be charged to an appropriation as if the transaction was monetary. (*) In this example it is assumed this purchase 
would be charged to the capital vote B14A. However, depending on the department and the asset purchased, the following authority 
codes could be used: B11A - Program Vote, B12A Operating Vote, and A131 Spending of amounts equivalent to proceeds from 
disposal of surplus Crown assets. "D321- Proceeds from disposal of crown assets" is used for the remaining debits and credits 
to reflect proceeds received by the Department. There is no impact on the authority side for the accounts payable but the 
system requires that a code be used, in this case it would be "R300- All other assets and liabilities"</p><p><strong>Object coding rationale:</strong> With respect to economic objects the exchange reflects the acquisition of an 
asset and the disposition of the asset. "1249- Other equipment and parts" is used to reflect the purchase of the equipment 
(XYZ). "4843-Sales of surplus Crown assets to outside parties" reflects the net disposal value and proceeds received for 
the asset given up - equipment (ABC). "6299-Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability Accounts" is used establish an accounts 
payable.</p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement Presentation and Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>None</p></section><section anchor="9.8" title="9.8 Transfers *"><h4>Introduction</h4><p><strong>For appropriation purposes</strong>, transfers that are grants, contributions or repayable contributions are 
charged to either a Grants and Contribution vote or a Program Expenditures vote.</p><p><strong>For accrual accounting purposes</strong>, it is necessary to differentiate among grants and contributions and 
repayable contributions.</p><p><em>Grants and contributions</em> are transfers of money and/or goods or services from the government to an individual, 
an organization or another government for which the federal government does not:</p><ul><li>receive any goods or services directly in return;</li><li>expect to be repaid; or</li><li>expect a financial return;</li></ul><p><em>Repayable contributions</em> are those transfers whereby the recipient is expected to repay the amount or the government 
expects to receive a financial return. The terms may specify a calendar date or dates for repayment, or may describe the 
particular time(s) or circumstances(s) that will determine repayment. (PS 3050.07)</p><p>Repayable contributions are further classified as unconditionally repayable and conditionally repayable. They require 
separate treatment for recording and reporting under accrual accounting.</p><ul><li><em>Unconditionally repayable contributions (URCs)</em> are contributions that must 
  be repaid without qualification. The contribution agreement contains specific repayment terms that set out the time and 
  amount of payment(s) due. URCs are in substance loans receivables.</li><li><em>Conditionally repayable contributions (CRCs)</em> are contributions, all or part 
  of which are repayable, if conditions specified in the contribution agreement come into being.</li></ul><p>Advance payments of all transfers shall be recorded as a financial asset until such time as the expense recognition criteria 
have been met.</p><p>All transfers of goods and/or services shall be recorded at the fair value of the asset or service given up.</p><p>For the accounting treatment of the following types of transfers see the following sections of the manual:</p><p>1. Grants and Contributions- see Grants and Contribution section under the Expenses section of the manual</p><p>2. Repayable Contributions</p><ol class="lower-alpha"><li>Unconditional Repayable Contributions - See Loans Receivable Section</li><li>Conditional Repayable Contributions - See Conditional Repayable Contributions Section.</li></ol><h4>References</h4><ul><li><em><a href="/pol/doc-eng.aspx?id=13525">Policy on Transfer Payments</a></em></li><li>TBAS 3.2 Transfers (Grants and Contributions)</li><li>PS 3050, 3410</li></ul><h4>9.8.1 Conditional Repayable Contributions</h4><p><strong>Authorities Perspective:</strong></p><p>A contribution is a conditional transfer payment to an individual or organization for a specified purpose pursuant to 
a contribution agreement that is subject to being accounted for and audited (<em>Transfer Payment Policy)</em>. Furthermore, 
a contribution, which includes repayable contributions can be conditional or unconditional depending on the requirement 
to repay.</p><p>For appropriation purposes repayable contributions are charged to either a Grants and Contribution vote or a Program 
Expenditures vote.</p><p><strong>Accrual Accounting Perspective:</strong></p><p>Conditionally repayable contributions (CRCs) are contributions, all or part of which are repayable, if conditions specified 
in the contribution agreement come into being, e.g. certain level of sales.</p><p>CRCs are distinct from unconditionally repayable contributions (URCs). The latter contains specific repayment terms that 
set out the time and amount of payment(s) due. These are in substance loans. See Loans Receivable Section of the manual.</p><p>CRCs shall be accounted for in accordance with PS 3410. They <strong>shall be recognized</strong><strong>as an</strong><strong>expense</strong> in the department's Statement of Operations in the period that the events giving rise to the transfer 
occurred, as long as:</p><ol class="lower-alpha"><li>the transfer is authorized;</li><li>eligibility criteria, if any, have been met by the recipient; and,</li><li>a reasonable estimate of the amount can be made</li></ol><p><strong>Contingent Recoveries</strong></p><p>Conditionally repayable contributions (CRCs) are contingencies that may qualify as contingent recoveries.</p><p>A contingency is defined as an existing condition or situation involving uncertainty as to possible gain or loss to an 
enterprise that will ultimately be resolved when one or more future events occur or fail to occur. Contingent recoveries 
are claims or rights to receive assets when existence is uncertain but may become valid eventually.</p><p>Contingent recoveries are not accrued in financial statements. Nevertheless, disclosure of the existence of a contingent 
recovery which is considered likely to be realized provides useful information and would, therefore, be included in a note 
to the financial statements.</p><p>When the existence of a contingent recovery, which has not been accrued, is disclosed in a note to the financial statements, 
the following information should be included:</p><ol class="lower-alpha"><li>The nature of the contingency; and</li><li>An estimate of the amount of the contingent recovery... or a statement that such an estimate cannot be made.</li></ol><p>Once it is certain that full or partial repayment is required, departments will set up a receivable and reduce the transfer 
expenses of the current period. Appropriate valuation allowances would be recorded.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li><em><a href="/pol/doc-eng.aspx?id=13525">Policy on Transfer Payments</a></em></li><li>TBAS 3.2 Transfers (Grants and Contributions)</li><li>PS 3410</li></ul><h4>Scenario A - Conditional Repayable Contributions.</h4><p>Department makes a contribution of $500,000 to a company involved in innovative research and development projects (the 
contribution is for capital assistance) and is repayable if conditions specified in the contribution agreement come into 
being. Conditions are likely to be met and a portion of the money is paid back.</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><p>1) To record disbursement of $500,000 CRC to a company</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>DR Transfer Payment Expense</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>500 000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>511XX</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B15A(*)</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>2185</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"><p>CR Accounts Payable</p></th><td class="alignTopRight"><p>500,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>21111</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>6299</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>(See section on Accounts Payable for the entries required for settlement of accounts payable)</p></div><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> Conditional repayable contributions are recorded as an expense since there is 
no assurance that any portion of the disbursement will be returned. An accounts payable is set up for the corresponding 
amount owing to the company.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> In this example the CRC is charged to the B15A(*) - Grant and Contribution 
vote but depending on the department B11A - Program Vote could be used as well. Since accounts payable has no impact on 
appropriations, R300 is used.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale</strong>: In this example transfer payments to industry for research and development were made 
for conditionally - recoverable payments for capital assistance, therefore 2185 is used. However depending on who the recipient 
of the CRC is the appropriate object would be used. "6299- Net Increase or Decrease to Other Liability accounts" should 
be used to indicate the establishment of the accounts payable.</p><h4>Scenario B - Conditions of Repayment Likely to be Met.</h4><p>1) Conditions of the repayment likely to be met, therefore note disclosure of contingent recovery is required.</p><div class="indent1"><p>No Journal Entry required. Only note disclosure of contingent recovery</p><div class="indent1"><p><em>"The Department makes contributions to industry involved in innovative research and development projects that 
    are repayable if conditions specified in the contribution agreement come into being. Based on the likelihood of those 
    conditions being met, a contingent recovery of $100,000 has been estimated to be realized in the future".</em></p></div></div><h4>Scenario C - Conditions of Repayment ARE Met.</h4><p>1) Conditions are met and a portion of the transfer ($100,000) is to be repaid.</p><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><th scope="col" class="alignTop" colspan="2"> </th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AMT($)</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>FRA</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>AUTH</strong></p></th><th scope="col" class="alignTopRight"><p><strong>OBJ</strong></p></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop">
 </th><td class="alignTopLeft"><p>DR Accounts Receivable for refunds of program expenses</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>11231</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>R300</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>5399</p></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="alignTop"> </th><td class="alignTopLeft"><p>CR Transfer Payment Expense</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>100,000</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>511XX</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>E500</p></td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>4731</p></td></tr></table><div class="indent1"><p>(See section on Accounts Receivable for the entries required for settlement of accounts receivable.)</p></div><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> Once it is certain that full or partial repayment is required, departments will 
set up a receivable and reduce the transfer expenses of the current period.</p><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> Since accounts receivable has no impact on appropriations, R300 is used. 
E500 is used to record revenue from this source for authority purposes.</p><p><strong>Object Rationale:</strong> To indicate the net impact on accounts receivable"5399-Net Change to Accounts Receivable" 
is used. "4731- Repayment of Recoverable Items/ Contribution recoveries" is used to capture the revenue associated with 
the repayment of this conditional repayment.</p><p><em>Please note: In the event the Department feels there is a possibility of the company not paying the receivable an 
appropriate allowance would be set up. See Accounts Receivable Section.</em></p><h4>Departmental Financial Statement Presentation and Disclosure Requirements</h4><p>Conditional repayable contributions will be recorded as expenses in the Department's Statement of Operations.</p><p>When the existence of a contingent recovery, which has not been accrued, is disclosed in a note to the financial statements, 
the following information should be included:</p><ol class="lower-alpha"><li>The nature of the contingency; and</li><li>An estimate of the amount of the contingent recovery... or a statement that such an estimate cannot be made.</li></ol><p>When conditions are met such that contingent recoveries will be realized, these receivables will be recorded under the 
heading Financial Assets in the Department's Statement of Financial Position.</p></section><section anchor="9.9" title="9.9 Funds Administered by Departments on Behalf of OGDs"><h4>Introduction</h4><p>This is an administrative arrangement whereby one department provides payment requisition functions or deposit functions 
on behalf of another department. The department providing the deposit functions on behalf of the other department is called 
the SPENDING DEPARTMENT.</p><p>It should be noted that this is different from a cost sharing arrangement or a group purchasing arrangement.</p><p>The correct use of the Internal/External (I/E) code is not self-evident for all transactions described in this section 
of the manual. Therefore, this section includes specific direction on the mandatory use of the code. This code is important 
for consolidations that are done at a government-wide level by the Receiver General.</p><h4>References</h4><ul><li><a href="/pol/doc-eng.aspx?id=12191"><em>Interdepartmental Settlements Policy</em></a></li><li><a href="http://publiservice.pwgsc.gc.ca/rg/text/recgen-e.html">RG Manual, Chapter 10, Section 10.8.6 Advances to Other Government Departments</a></li><li><a href="http://publiservice.pwgsc.gc.ca/rg/text/oldrg-e.html">RG Directive on Year-End Procedures</a></li></ul><h4>Scenario A</h4><p>One Department requests that another government department requisition payments on its behalf for goods and/or services. 
It was estimated that for the current year that this activity would be $100,000. The funding department advanced this amount 
to the spending department. Periodically an accounting for the use of the funds is provided to the funding department from 
the spending department. For purposes of this Scenario , $40,000 was spent by the spending department with an additional 
$15,000 accrued at year-end.</p><p>Note: the numbering of the entries indicates the time sequence of their performance (i.e. entry 1a would occur before 
entry 1b).</p><h4>Journal Entries</h4><table class="table table-bordered table-condensed"><tr><td colspan="7"><p><strong>FUNDING DEPARTMENT</strong></p></td></tr><tr><td class="alignTop" colspan="7"><p>1a) To record the amount of funds transferred to the Spending Department.</p></td></tr><tr><td class="alignTopRight"></td><td class="alignTopRight"></td><td class="alignTopRight"><strong>AMT($)</strong></td><td class="alignTopRight"><strong>FRA</strong></td><td class="alignTopRight"><strong>AUTH</strong></td><td class="alignTopRight"><strong>OBJ</strong></td><td class="alignTopRight"><strong>I/E</strong></td></tr><tr><td class="alignTopLeft">DR </td><td class="alignTopLeft">OGD Suspense Adv. </td><td class="alignTopRight">100,000 </td><td class="alignTopRight">11244 </td><td class="alignTopRight">B11A/B12A </td><td class="alignTopRight">5399 </td><td class="alignTopRight">I </td></tr><tr><td class="alignTopLeft">CR </td><td class="alignTopLeft">IS Credit Control Acct </td><td class="alignTopRight">100,000 </td><td class="alignTopRight">65DDD </td><td class="alignTopRight">0000 </td><td class="alignTopRight">9XXX </td><td class="alignTopRight">I </td></tr><tr><td class="alignTop" colspan="7"><p>DDD - Funding Department's department number<br></br>
    XXX - Spending Department's department number</p></td></tr><tr><td class="alignTop" colspan="7"><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> The Funding Department is giving the Spending Department $100,000 as an advance. 
    The expectation is that the funds will be spent by the spending department for the acquisition of goods and services 
    on behalf of the funding department. In the event the funds are not spent they must be returned, therefore the amount 
    is recorded as an interdepartmental receivable. The IS control account is credited for the amount paid to the Spending 
    Department.</p></td></tr><tr><td class="alignTop" colspan="7"><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> As required, the appropriation is charged at the point the transfer 
    is made as an advance to the spending department. Since the funds are to be used for goods and services on the Funding 
    Department's behalf, either B11A or B12A could be used depending on the Department's vote structure. The IS Control 
    Accounts have no impact on an appropriation so the authority code must be zero-filled.</p></td></tr><tr><td class="alignTop" colspan="7"><p><strong>Object Coding Rationale:</strong> To indicate the net impact on accounts receivable "5399-Net Change to Accounts 
    Receivable" is used. 9XXX is used for interdepartmental settlements and would be used to identify the Spending Department.</p></td></tr><tr><td class="alignTop" colspan="7"><p><strong>Internal/External Coding Rationale:</strong> All transactions through SPS/IS are considered to be Internal, 
    therefore an I is used.</p></td></tr><tr><td class="alignTop" colspan="7">
    2b) Spending Department provides information to the Funding Department regarding particulars of expenses incurred. 
      The Funding Department prepares an Internal Journal Voucher (JV<strong>)</strong> to record these transactions against 
      the applicable account(s). In this case, to is assumed that the entire $40,000 was for operating expenses.</td></tr><tr><td class="alignTopRight"></td><td class="alignTopRight"></td><td class="alignTopRight"><strong>AMT($)</strong></td><td class="alignTopRight"><strong>FRA</strong></td><td class="alignTopRight"><strong>AUTH</strong></td><td class="alignTopRight"><strong>OBJ</strong></td><td class="alignTopRight"><strong>I/E</strong></td></tr><tr><td class="alignTopLeft">DR </td><td class="alignTopLeft">Operating Expenses </td><td class="alignTopRight">40,000 </td><td class="alignTopRight">51321 </td><td class="alignTopRight">B11A/B12A </td><td class="alignTopRight">0xxx/1xxx </td><td class="alignTopRight">I/E </td></tr><tr><td class="alignTopLeft">CR </td><td class="alignTopLeft">OGD Suspense Adv. </td><td class="alignTopRight">40,000 </td><td class="alignTopRight">11244 </td><td class="alignTopRight"><p>B11A/B12A</p></td><td class="alignTopRight">5399 </td><td class="alignTopRight">I/E </td></tr><tr><td class="alignTop" colspan="7"><p><strong>FRA Coding Rationale:</strong> The Funding Department must record the cost of the goods and services on their 
    books. They will debit operating expenses for $40,000. Of the $100,000 given to the Spending Department $40,000 has 
    been spent on goods and services so the advance must be reduced by that amount.</p></td></tr><tr><td class="alignTop" colspan="7"><p><strong>Authority Coding Rationale:</strong> Since the appropriation was originally charged when the advance was 
    made to the funding department (in Scenario A Journal Entry 1), no new charge is required to the appropriation at this 
    point. To ensure there is no impact on the appropriations, the same authority code is used on the debit and credit side 
    of the entry.</p></td></tr><tr><td class="alignTop" colspan="7"><p><strong>Object Coding Rationale:</strong> To indicate the net impact on accounts receivable "5399-Net Change to Accounts 
    Receivable" is used. Depending the nature of the good or service acquired, the appropriate object of expenditure code 
    would be used. The object starting with 0 is for a service and an object starting with a 1 is for a good.</p></td></tr><tr><td class="alignTop" colspan="7"><p><strong>External or Internal Rationale:</strong> The code to use will depend upon whether the original transaction 
    for the goods and services by the Spending Department was internal or external.</p></td></tr><tr><td class="alignTop" colspan="7"><p><strong>Alternate Entries: </strong>The above entry can alternatively be recorded in two entries.</p></td></tr><tr><td class="alignTop" colspan="7"><p>3b) Funding Department is notified by Spending Department of $15,000 of year-end
